Heavy Guarding Like Facing a Great Enemy: Saarbrücken Begins Counting Ballots 38

Bayonets and Lights Shine Together; Results to be Revealed This Afternoon

Saar's Return to Germany a Foregone Conclusion; Four Matters Awaiting Decision by the League of Nations

The Saar region, including Saarbrücken, with a population of 800,000 and abundant coal mines, will know its fate tomorrow morning. The ballot counting began at 5 PM today at Saarbrücken, and will continue throughout the night. The results will be announced at 7 AM tomorrow (3 PM Shanghai time), at which time it will be known whether this 737-mile land will be returned to Germany, annexed to France, or remain under the administration of the League of Nations. As for rumors that 40,000 residents plan to move to France, members of the German Front dismiss this with a laugh. (Reuters, 14th)

According to official reports from Saarbrücken, Hitler's representative in the Saar, Mr. Bukel, will report to Hitler via radio immediately after the ballot results are announced. The entire German nation will be able to listen. The ballot boxes are being transported to the Saarbrücken hall, closely guarded by international police along the way. The hall, where the ballot boxes will be opened, is brightly lit like a film set. British police are responsible for security, heavily deployed around the perimeter. Bayonets on rifles gleam in the lamplight, and no one is allowed to linger nearby without special permission. However, stands for spectators and journalists have been prepared, and photographers are busy setting up their cameras. The ballot boxes have been kept sealed until today, when they will be opened under heavy guard, as if facing a great enemy. All members of the Saar Plebiscite Commission, representatives of the League of Nations, members of the Saar Governing Commission, representatives of Germany and France, as well as the commander and important officials of the international police force, will participate in the ballot counting tonight. The ballot boxes weigh a total of two tons, making transportation difficult, especially after the heavy snow. All industries in the Saar region will be suspended tomorrow to listen to the announcement of the voting results, essentially uniting all German people in the region as one family to celebrate a true people's festival. The Saar has been separated from Germany for fifteen years. If lost territory is recovered, wouldn't that be a great commemorative event? (National News Agency, 14th)

(Geneva) The Saar Plebiscite Commission telegraphed the Council of the League of Nations today, stating that the voting was very peaceful, with the people showing strict discipline and a calm demeanor. (National News Agency, 14th)

(London) The Saar vote has passed peacefully, and everyone is very satisfied. Geneva sees the hope for an early resolution of the overall situation as brighter than ever. All parties are now working to conclude this matter during this session of the League of Nations Council. (Reuters, 14th)

(Geneva) On the day of the Saar plebiscite, key officials of the League of Nations made special arrangements to work as usual on Sunday, and every hour they communicated with the Saar Plebiscite Commission via long-distance telephone to inquire about the progress of the voting and make it public. In general, the voting was very smooth, the order was very good, and the number of voters was very enthusiastic. A radio broadcasting machine was also installed in the Great Hall of the League of Nations, preparing to announce the voting results on Tuesday morning. The League of Nations Council will convene a meeting after the voting results are announced, and there are four matters to be discussed and decided: (1) To whom will the Saar belong in the future? (2) If, according to the current trend, the people of the Saar seem to have a unanimous tendency to merge with Germany, and if the voting results require a merger with Germany, then set the date of the merger. (3) On what date will the international troops withdraw after the complete merger of the Saar becomes a reality? (4) How should public officials in the Saar region who cannot continue to be employed by Germany be subsidized after the merger of the Saar and Germany? This matter will be negotiated and coordinated by the German government and the current Saar government, and then formally recognized by the League of Nations. (National News Agency, 14th)

Ballot Boxes Escorted to Saarbrücken 39

After the plebiscite in Saarbrücken concluded last night, the ballot boxes were collected from various locations by international troops and transported to the Saarbrücken building for tabulation. Large crowds gathered to watch, not dispersing throughout the night. Starting at 9 PM, several trucks began transporting the ballot boxes from various polling stations to the Saarbrücken building. This building is the property of the Evangelical Church of Saarbrücken and is built of red brick. Saarbrücken police are currently responsible for maintaining order, prohibiting curious onlookers from entering, only allowing them to stand at a considerable distance outside the building. The vote count will take place in the main hall, lasting the entire day. A large number of public officials, journalists, and film photographers crowded the steps at the entrance. The magnesium lamps of the photographers flashed, creating an interesting contrast with the moving crowd. Two British soldiers, wearing steel helmets, guarded the gate, their rifles equipped with bayonets. Another team of Italian soldiers surrounded several machine guns, providing protection outside the building. At the entrance to the vehicle passage, there were also six soldiers guarding, each with a bayonet on their rifle. Before long, the first truck carrying the ballot boxes arrived, drove through the passage, and stopped in front of the hall. Soldiers also guarded the hall door. After the ballot boxes were unloaded, they were densely arranged in the hall, waiting to be counted. (Havas, 14th)

All 862 ballot boxes in the Saar region of Saarbrücken were transported to the Saarbrücken building by 5 AM this morning. Police and British troops guarded the outside of the door, rifles equipped with bayonets. The ballot counting is scheduled to begin at 5 PM this afternoon and is expected to be completed by tomorrow morning. A total of 55,000 voters from foreign countries participated in the voting, and some of them have already departed last night, while the rest are leaving one after another. It is estimated that all of them will be able to leave by tonight. The railway authorities have made proper arrangements for transportation, so although there are many travelers, there are no delays or other accidents. (Havas, 14th)

Over 70% Voted to Return to Germany 40

The voting situation was very calm. The 86 polling stations closed at 8 PM tonight. Of the 539,300 voters, 98% braved the wind and snow to vote at the ballot boxes. According to general opinion, those who voted in favor of the Saar's return to Germany will account for at least 75%. However, the leader of the German Front claimed that the final election results will show that 85% of voters voted in favor of the Saar's return to Hitler's rule. (National News Agency, 14th)

Hitler Quietly Awaits Results 41

(Berlin) All German newspapers unanimously predict that Germany will win a great victory in the Saar region plebiscite. The number of votes in favor of merging with Germany estimated by some newspapers, when added together, exceeds the total number of votes. Although the newspapers consider some of the measures taken by the Saar Administrative Commission and the Plebiscite Commission to maintain order to be fair, they believe that the reason why the plebiscite did not cause any incidents is due to the German Front. The German newspapers previously said that the number of Saar people who supported maintaining the status quo was very small, but now they say that a large number of those who supported maintaining the status quo have secretly fled the country. Leader and Chancellor Hitler is now in Berchtesgaden, quietly awaiting the results of the Saar vote on Tuesday. Foreign Minister Neurath may go to the Bavarian Alps on Tuesday to discuss the issues that arise after the plebiscite with Hitler. Semi-official optimists hope that the League of Nations Council can make a decision within this week. Although Germany has refused to attend the Council meeting, the German consul in Geneva may participate in the negotiations if necessary. (Havas, 14th)

Many Post-Return Issues 42

If the Saar region merges with Germany, the most important issues to be resolved are as follows: (1) The issue of returning the Saar mines to Germany. (2) How to replace the French francs currently used in the Saar with marks. (3) How to change the Saar's economic system so that it does not conflict with Germany's economic system after the Saar returns. All of the above issues need to be resolved. Germany will probably seek to amend the Franco-German commercial treaty, at least during the transition period. When the Saar returns to Germany, the German government will promulgate special laws to restore the Saar region's sovereignty, and the area will be incorporated into the German Palatinate region. In addition, laws regarding the tariff system, currency restoration, and various economic measures are also being prepared. These laws will take effect from the date of the Saar's declaration of sovereignty restoration. Semi-official figures believe that Hitler will deliver a speech on Tuesday, when the results of the Saar region's vote are announced. (Havas, 14th)

Unexpectedly Orderly 43

When the polling stations in Saarbrücken closed at 8 PM last night, it was estimated that 97% of the total number of voters had voted. Everything was peaceful everywhere, and the voters were very orderly. In the morning, voters gathered outside the polling stations, but in the afternoon, the polling stations felt empty. The city hall was also one of the polling stations, and crowds gathered in front of it to watch the police move the ballot boxes to the motor vehicles outside the door. When the police came out, the crowd cheered loudly, mixed with shouts of "Heil Hitler!" and performed the Nazi salute. When the open car began to drive to Saarbrücken, the crowd sang German national anthems and party songs to express their joy. The ballot boxes in Saarbrücken were all sent to the Saarbrücken building, mostly transported by train, and heavily guarded by the military. By late night, the ballot boxes were delivered one after another. As far as is known, no one who voted in favor of returning the Saar to Germany was disqualified for shouting "Heil Hitler!" or performing the Nazi salute. As the elders voted, children gathered in the streets, throwing snowballs for fun. An Italian military vehicle, equipped with a machine gun, was repeatedly hit by snowballs while patrolling the city of Saarbrücken. At dusk, residents gathered in cafes and bars to discuss the day's voting. Many firmly believe that the Saar will be returned to Germany, and some fear the future. However, because the time for selling alcohol is limited, there is little expression of joy. (Reuters, 14th)

In the Saarbrücken plebiscite, the surnames of the voters were marked on the ballot boxes, placed side by side in order, so that voters could vote under the letter label of their respective surnames, which was quite convenient. However, because the German people, like the Chinese, have large families such as Zhang, Li, Chen, and Wang, special ballot boxes were added for the convenience of these people, such as "Schmidt," "Schneider," "Müller," and "Wagner." A certain Schmidt ballot box alone received 1,500 votes, and another received 1,400. Müller voted in the same place, and a certain Schneider ballot box also had more than 800 votes. (National News Agency, 13th)

Several Minor Disturbances Occurred 44

The orderly nature of this vote in Saarbrücken can be attributed to the strict discipline of the German Front. However, in Neunkirchen, an anti-Nazi threw a bomb at a branch office of the German Front, slightly injuring one person. Another anti-Nazi burned a swastika flag. Police arrested two immigrants and two communists. At the same time, France and the Netherlands closed their borders. (National News Agency, 14th)

The plebiscite in Saarbrücken has passed quietly, with only a few minor incidents to spice things up. A bomb was thrown into the German automobile club in Neunkirchen, which is the local Nazi headquarters. It is now believed that the bomber was a communist who also fired shots at the pursuers, injuring one person. One communist was arrested in Saar Louis. His apartment contained eight bombs, 200 hand grenades, and 60 pounds of explosives. An 82-year-old woman died at a polling station in Hostatte. It is not known whether she voted. (Reuters, 14th)

Ms. Meng Dunna Was the Last Person to Vote 45

Traveled Across the Ocean from Shanghai

Germans' Emphasis on Voting Rights is Evident Here

The last person to vote in the Saarbrücken plebiscite today was Ms. Meng Dunna. In order to vote, she departed from Shanghai, traveling 8,000 miles by plane, train, and ship. As a result, she was exhausted when she arrived here. When she arrived at her destination by car, she was beaming with joy after voting, as if to show that she had fulfilled her responsibility. (National News Agency, 13th)

A Chorus of Nazi Party Songs 46

When the city hall took away the ballot boxes in Saarbrücken, the German Front made a demonstration. When the first ballot box appeared in front of the city hall, the song "Germany Above All" began to be sung. A Nazi leader sang the first verse, followed by the crowd singing "Saar Song" and "Nazi Party Song," all voices singing in unison. In the evening, the Nazi Party headquarters declared that the propaganda campaign was coming to an end, and the entire group went to the municipal theater to watch the play "William Tell" (a hero from the early 14th century). This play is a work by Schiller, and the singing was very noisy. The main oppressor in the play is Gessler, and William Tell opposes Gessler. During today's performance, the crowd mocked Gessler to make fun of him. Although William Tell is regarded as a national hero by everyone, opinions differ on his resistance. Some regard him as resisting foreign oppression, while others regard him as opposing Hitler's dictatorship. But the theater situation was still peaceful last night. At the request of the German Front, the theater manager deleted the most rebellious verses in the play. Usually, when these verses were sung, people would fight each other, but now they have been deleted, so there is less noise. After the play, the staff of the headquarters accompanied the crowd to the Saarbrücken building, where the ballot boxes were gathered. At midnight, the whole city was quiet, with no flags or lights, which was contrary to expectations. The streets were almost empty. On the night of the plebiscite, all the people of the Saar went to sleep together. (Havas, 14th)

Opposition Expresses Protest 47

Voting Suppressed by Nazis, Violates Conditions of Freedom and Secrecy

The leaders of the status quo faction in Saarbrücken, Plang and Volte, invited foreign journalists tonight to express their protest against the course of the plebiscite. Plang declared that the Saar police exercised their duties, obviously with fraudulent circumstances. The police secretly followed the orders of the Nazi Party and did not patrol. Many international troops also did not patrol, so the residents had the impression that the vote had been controlled by the Nazi Party's security and storm troopers. In addition, cleaners and fire brigades were also mostly inclined to the German Front. Leaflets were distributed throughout the Saar region, saying that the socialist leader Plang, the Catholic leader Hoffmann, and the communist leader Volte had fled. In fact, all this was fabricated by the Nazi trade union, because these three people did attend and entertained foreign journalists tonight. Plang also said that voters from Germany to the Saar region must first swear an oath to vote in favor of the Nazi Party, so the leaders of the status quo faction solemnly declared that because of the above circumstances, this vote cannot be considered a free and secret vote. The League of Nations has a binding obligation to hold votes under conditions of freedom and secrecy, but since this obligation cannot be fulfilled, the results of the vote should be reserved. Plang also declared that he would negotiate with the League of Nations. Communist leader Volte told foreign journalists that he firmly opposed Hitler to the end, saying that if international agencies cannot protect human freedom, then rather than endure oppression, we should take the most extreme measures to achieve the final goal. (Havas, 13th)

German Ambassador Papen Filled with Emotion 48

Former German Prime Minister, now Minister to Austria, Papen, resided in the capital of Switzerland and owned property in Voltaire, Saar. He came to the Saar with his family to fulfill his voting obligations and participate in the plebiscite. A reporter from the Swiss Telegraph Agency interviewed him and obtained his comments, in which he said that the European war or peace will be decided by this plebiscite. He declined to predict the voting results, only saying that the results would be unusually important and could create a new relationship between France and Germany, with a view to contributing to European peace. Finally, Papen mentioned the garden he had built in Voltaire and could not help but sigh, saying, "Today, people are dominated by political desires and compete endlessly. Don't they see that the joy of these forests and springs is so worthy of attachment?" (Havas, 13th)

Netherlands and France Determined to Accept Fugitives 49

The Hague The Dutch government has decided that if the Saar region's voting results favor merging with Germany, anti-Nazi people in the Saar region, except for those who cannot be accommodated, will be allowed to flee to the Netherlands. (Havas, 13th)

Saarbrücken A large number of people have now started to leave the country, because those who voted against the Saar's merger with Germany are deeply afraid of unfavorable consequences after the Saar is handed over to Germany. Therefore, they are moving to France. However, the number of people leaving the Saar today is very small compared to the number of people who will leave after the Saar is officially returned to Germany. It is estimated that 40,000 people will leave in the future. (National News Agency, 14th)

Arguments of Various Newspapers 50

Saarbrücken Although there is no official news about the results of the plebiscite, the Nazi newspapers believe that the Saar's return to Germany is a "fait accompli." The Saar newspaper said, "The current struggle has come to an end, and people of all levels are relieved." On the other hand, the newspapers of the socialist and communist joint front expressed dissatisfaction with the attitude of the League of Nations institutions towards Nazi activities yesterday. They all said that the responsibility for maintaining order in Saarbrücken was actually in the hands of the Nazi Party's security team and storm troopers. As the New Saar Post said, "The German Front directs its members to swagger through the city, saying that their intention is not to provoke, but also to threaten voters. How can this be?" The Ordinary Guidance newspaper said, "The impression felt by neutral observers is that the order is well-established and not chaotic. But who knows that this is only a superficial situation? The German Front is exerting secret pressure on voters, creating an environment of hesitation, panic, and fear. Where is the so-called free voting?" (Havas, 14th)

Zhu Fuguang Public Funeral Yesterday 51

Public Memorial Service Held the Day Before Yesterday; Zhang Ji Read the Eulogy

(Xi'an) A telegram from Sanyuan: The public funeral of Zhu Fuguang, a revolutionary pioneer in Shaanxi, will be held at 10 AM on the 14th in Sanyuan County. Yu Youren, Shao Lizi, Zhang Ji, and leaders of party, government, and military organs in the provincial capital held a public memorial service at 4 PM on the 13th at Zhu's cemetery in the southern suburbs of Sanyuan. Shao Lizi presided over the ceremony, Yu reported Zhu's deeds, and Zhang Puquan and others gave speeches, and read the eulogies from the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and Chairman Chiang. About 2,000 people attended. The ceremony ended at 5:30 PM. Shao and others stayed at the Minzhi Elementary School and will return to the province after the public funeral on the 14th. (Central News Agency, 13th)

Yan's Father's Funeral Yesterday 52

Xu and He Represented Lin and Chiang in Holding the Coffin Ropes

(Taiyuan) He Yingqin and Huang Fu, representing Yang Tingpu, were guided by Xu Yongchang, Jia Jingde, Zhu Shouhong, and Guang Ronglu this morning, and went to the riverside by car to pay tribute to Yan's father on behalf of Lin and Chiang and to hold the coffin ropes to the funeral. Yan held a family memorial service this morning and was buried at 2 PM in the afternoon. There were still many people going to the funeral from Bing today. According to a telephone call from the riverside, Yan has prepared a residence for He in Xihui Village and plans to keep He for a few days to discuss everything. All organs and schools in Bing City were ordered to fly flags at half-mast for one day, and entertainment venues suspended performances during the day to mourn Yan's father. Representatives of the party and government of Sui Province returned to Bing after paying tribute yesterday and will visit Jinci guided by Wang Danjiu, secretary of the Sui Provincial Government, and will return to Sui tomorrow morning. (Special Dispatch, 14th)

(Taiyuan) He Yingqin and his wife visited Jinci on the morning of the 13th. At 7 PM, Xu Yongchang and other military and political figures in Jin Province held a public banquet. He went to the riverside on the morning of the 14th to pay tribute to Yan's father and can leave Bing for Ping on the 15th. The 13th was the day of the memorial service for Yan's father. Five hundred representatives from all over the country and representatives from various organs and groups in Jin Province went to the riverside to pay tribute. The funeral will be held on the morning of the 14th. Xu Yongchang represents Chairman Lin, He Yingqin represents Chairman Chiang, and Yang Tingpu represents Huang Fu in holding the coffin ropes. Hebei Construction Department Plans to Request Funds to Repair the Yellow River Dyke in Southern Hebei 53

Changyuan County Magistrate Telegraphed About Dangerous Works

(Tianjin) The Hebei Construction Department plans to telegraph the Central Government to allocate 1.4 million yuan to thicken the Yellow River Dyke in Southern Hebei this spring, increasing the thickness and width by one time to prevent floods, and to build various water control projects to ensure safety. (Special Dispatch, 14th)

(Tianjin) Zhang Qinglu, the magistrate of Changyuan County, telegraphed the province, saying that the Taihang Dyke was being scoured by ice floes and was extremely dangerous. It is estimated that the entire rescue project requires more than 19,800 yuan, and the cost of preventing ice floes, to replace relief with work, requires 5,000 yuan. Please allocate the funds quickly. The province will wait for the 15th regular meeting to decide. (Special Dispatch, 14th)

Hubei Provincial Government Ordered to Expedite Relief Work in Bandit Areas 56

(Hankou) The headquarters ordered the provincial government to expedite relief work in the bandit areas: (1) Order all wealthy farmers who have fled to return to their villages, organize local militias, and assist poor farmers; otherwise, their abandoned wasteland will be distributed to poor farmers for cultivation. (2) Engage in the resettlement of refugees and legally regulate the rent of wealthy farmers, which must not exceed 50%, and the government will set up loan offices to provide funds. As for past feuds, they must be handled with leniency to prevent unrest. Other matters such as immigration and reclamation will be properly drafted by various departments and submitted for approval. January 14th, Reuter's Special Commercial Dispatch

(Gold and Silver) ▲The London gold price today is 141 shillings and 11 pence, up by 3 and a half pence.

▲The London silver price today rose by .0625, with the spot price at 24 and a half pence and the futures price at 24 and .625 pence. The market is stable, with purchases from the United States and trading by speculators.

▲The Bombay large bar silver market was quiet today, with the spot closing price at 64 rupees and 15 annas, up 7 annas.

(Exchange Rates) ▲In the London foreign exchange market this morning, the US dollar was in slightly higher demand, and the British pound showed a slight downward trend. The opening exchange rate between the British pound and the US dollar was $4.90625, which was .125 lower than the closing rate on Saturday and Sunday. It later narrowed significantly. The most recent price is $4.900625, which is .05625 lower than the opening price. One US dollar equals 4 shillings and .0973 British pounds. ▲The opening rate between the British pound and the French franc was 74 francs and 21, which was 7 pounds lower than on Saturday and Sunday. It then fell by another 6 pounds to 74 francs and 15. This price remained unchanged until the time of dispatch.

▲In the New York foreign exchange market, the British pound was weak. The opening exchange rate between the US dollar and the British pound was $4.89875, which was .0875 lower than the closing rate on Saturday and Sunday. It then fell by another .0375 to $4.895.

(Cotton and Wheat) ▲New York Cotton: Before the cotton market opened, it was generally expected that the market conditions would not change much. However, after the opening, there were many transactions, and prices rose by 2 to 4 points. Industry insiders still bought a lot, mostly for settlement purposes. Prices gradually increased slightly. ▲New York Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened steadily, with no change in prices. Before long, due to profit-taking by bulls, the market price fell slightly. The weather is very cold, but it is necessary to consider that European demand may decrease.

▲Bombay Cotton: Today's cotton market saw futures traders buying in large quantities, while Japanese and European exporters sold. The closing price for the April-May delivery of white Broach cotton was 140 rupees and 25, down 2 and a half rupees. Market sentiment at the close was stable.

▲Liverpool Wheat: The wheat market made slight progress today. At 1:00 PM, the price for the May delivery was 5 shillings and 1 and a half pence, up .125. ▲Liverpool Cotton: In the cotton market today, at 1:00 PM, the price for the May delivery was 6.8, up 2 points.

(Rubber) ▲London: Market conditions were stable today. The trading price for the April-June delivery at noon was 6.75 pence, the same as Saturday and Sunday.

▲New York: Trading was light at the opening today, and prices rose slightly by one pound. (Securities) ▲New York: Before the market opened today, a factor favorable to market conditions was that the steel industry reported that steel mills were operating at 45.5% of capacity last week. Therefore, the steel industry is gradually becoming profitable. It is estimated that steel mills in the Youngstown area will reach 5% of their capacity this week. The factor unfavorable to market conditions is the panic regarding the gold standard issue. Although it had a great impact on the securities market on Friday and Saturday, it continues to be a concern. The securities market opened this morning with stable market conditions, with only slight fluctuations. It is said that the downward trend has reached a level that could attract buying interest, but the market does not yet appear to be calm. According to news this morning, a group called the United Automobile Shareholders Committee is launching a movement to directly contact automobile shareholders, advocating that the major American automobile companies be merged into a single large group.

According to a Reuter's report, the results of the gold standard issue are still uncertain, and the securities market is still subject to its influence. Although some people believe that the downward trend is already significant, it is generally expected that if President Roosevelt does not take any unexpected actions, securities prices will continue to decline. The market opened this morning with relatively stable market conditions, and the upward and downward trends were not significant. However, the overall sentiment remains fearful. Market conditions today are expected to be mixed. The market prices of New York securities are listed below:

Ministry of Industry Rectifies Fishermen's Association Organizations 66

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industry stated that the purpose of fishermen's associations is to enhance the knowledge and skills of fishermen, improve their lives, and develop production. In areas with prosperous fisheries, those that have not established fishermen's associations should be urged to organize them. Those that have already established fishermen's associations but have unsound organizations, frequent disputes, and no achievements should be guided and rectified in accordance with the law. The Ministry of Industry has formulated eight points of attention for the competent supervisory authorities of fishermen's associations and has issued a circular to the provincial and municipal governments along the Yangtze River and the coast, as well as the Weihaiwei Administrative Office, ordering them to comply. (14th Dispatch)

When they went to the Audit Department, five representatives, including Zou Zhaojing, were selected from the forty-plus people. Research Report on the Silver Issue 72

(Nanjing) It was reported that Washington D.C. reported that the Chinese government and Jinling University would publish a report on the silver issue. It has been learned that the Chinese government and Jinling University have no joint publication of the so-called research report on the silver issue. It may refer to the report of the Silver Price and Commodity Price Discussion Committee organized by the Ministry of Industry last year. According to Xu Shilian, the chairman of the committee, the Ministry of Industry, in order to understand the impact of rising silver prices on national agriculture, industry, and commerce, hired Chen Bingquan and American Buick Lewis to form a discussion committee. Since February last year, the discussion committee collected actual numerical materials and completed an English report in five chapters at the end of December. It has been undertaken by the Commercial Press for printing and will be published by the end of February this year. The Chinese translation will also be printed. The book is based entirely on facts and statistics and is a reference for studying the silver issue. The news transmitted from Washington D.C. may be a misrepresentation of this matter. (14th Dispatch)

Yu Xuezhong Cables Beijing, Urging Blocking of Yellow River Breach 100

No Dry Land Remains Within Changyuan City; Part of the Hutuo River Project Completed

Tianjin Dispatch: The post-disaster works for blocking the Yellow River breach in southern Hebei, since the abolition of the Yellow River Post-Disaster Works Office, has been the responsibility of the Yellow River Conservancy Bureau. There are four breaches in total: (1) Chelezhuang, (2) Jiugulu, (3) Xiangliwan, and (4) Buzhai. According to the survey by the Conservancy Bureau, these four breaches are easy to construct but difficult to execute. This is because the water flow from the Yellow River breach originates from the Guantaigou in Henan Province. The water flows through the old course of the Yellow River, rushes into the depressions, and directly reaches the four breaches, inundating the area around Changyuan County. To block the four breaches, it is necessary to first block Guantaigou to cut off the water flow; otherwise, it will be difficult to achieve success. Previously, the Central Yellow Disaster Relief Commission stipulated that the funds for blocking Guantaigou alone would require more than 110,000 yuan. The difficulty and magnitude of the project can be imagined. Unexpectedly, as the project was underway, a sudden surge of cold water caused the water level in Guantaigou to rise sharply. The torrential flow caused the water that had receded from the vicinity of Changyuan to rise again by two to three feet, or even four to five feet. The workers at the four breaches were ordered by the Conservancy Bureau and the Magistrate of Changyuan County to gather at Guantaigou day and night to rush the blocking, in order to prevent danger. However, the disaster relief materials needed locally, such as sorghum stalks, sacks, and sand, were not easily obtained. The willow branches in the surrounding areas had all been cut down. Furthermore, the project funds exceeded the budget, causing a sense of financial strain. Although the Conservancy Bureau and the Magistrate were desperately trying to block the flow, the situation remained critical. Fortunately, the water stopped rising on the 8th of this month. If the water level drops slightly in the future, the people of Dongming, Changyuan, and Puyang counties may not suffer another disaster. The accumulated water outside Changyuan City, after prolonged soaking, has connected with the water inside the city. The water depth reaches thirteen or fourteen feet in the deepest places, and eight or nine feet even in the shallowest. The four hundred villages around the city are all in the middle of the water. The higher ground in the county seat, with four streets, had never been flooded before, but now there is no place that is not submerged. Chairman Yu Xuezhong of Hebei Province has sent consecutive telegrams reporting the disaster and requesting funds. In addition to ordering the Yellow Disaster Relief Committee and the Construction Department to appropriately allocate funds for emergency dispatch to the construction site, he sent a telegram to the Central Yellow Disaster Relief Committee and the Henan Provincial Government on the 11th, requesting the rapid allocation of funds to block and repair Guantaigou, in order to prevent the submergence of the three counties in southern Hebei.

Hu Yuanhui, Director of the Hebei Construction Department, recently inspected the Hutuo River irrigation project site with Lu Muting, Director of the Finance Department. They returned to Tianjin the night before last from Lingshou. According to Hu, seventy percent of the water diversion project in the high-water area of the Hutuo River has been completed. All the machinery used has been ordered from England and Germany and is expected to arrive at the construction site for use in early next month. Once the project is completed, the irrigation project will be fully completed and is scheduled to begin releasing water on May 1 this year. Approximately 120,000 mu of land in Lingshou and Zhengding counties can be irrigated. The area was originally very barren, but will become fertile farmland, benefiting the people. The local farmers mainly grow cotton. In the future, the department will guide the improvement of cotton varieties to increase yields. Since the department merged into the Department of Industry, the first thing it has focused on is the improvement of cotton varieties. Most cotton farmers in the cotton-producing areas of the province are clinging to old methods. The department will vigorously promote American cotton varieties in order to improve the quality of cotton production. (11th)

Discovery of Crystal Mine in Luotian, She County 101

Sparkling and Dazzling; the Larger Ones are Like Fingers

Huizhou dispatch: Crystal is quartz crystallized from amethyst, a precious and valuable substance. Although China is rich in mineral resources, crystal mines are rare. In previous years, they have been produced in Majiang, Fujian Province, and Guyang, Suiyuan Province, but the crystals were not fully transparent and were not considered perfect. The mountains in Huizhou are crisscrossed, and the flowing sand often forms minerals. Recently, crystal stones were discovered in the mountains behind Luotian Village in the northern part of She County. The shapes are like geometric polyhedra, sparkling and dazzling. The smaller ones are like rice grains, and the larger ones are like fingers. Large pieces are very rare. According to the villagers, the mountains are rugged with numerous strange rocks, and there are many white stones similar to un-crystallized, non-transparent crystals. Without expert investigation, it is unknown whether there are large quantities of crystal mines in the area. (January 8th)

Burglaries in Songjiang during Winter Defense Period Alarm Various Townships 102

The homes of farmers Zhang Changyu and Zhang Jinghua along the railway in Cangqiao South Zhujia Village in this city were suddenly raided by seven or eight armed bandits around 8 PM on the 13th. They looted over 1,400 cash coins and a long gown. Before leaving, they fired a shot as a warning. Upon receiving the report, the County Public Security Bureau immediately dispatched a special task force and police from the Second and Third Precincts to pursue, but the bandits had already escaped without a trace. The home of Xu Xiaoguan in Pan Ku Village, Caojing Sixth Ward, was also raided by multiple bandits around 10 PM on the 11th. They looted cloth clothing and fur robes, etc. The homeowner's grandmother, Madam Wan, and mother, Madam Feng, were both scalded on the head and face, causing extreme pain. Some of the bandits were carrying guns. Furthermore, the homes of Fan Shouyun and Fan Bosheng, villagers of Wangjia Ku Village in Sijing, were also robbed on the night of the 10th. However, as the loot was insufficient, they forced Bosheng's younger brother, Yougen, to lead them to the home of Bao Chengzhang in the same village, tricking him into opening the door and carrying out the robbery. They looted over 130 silver dollars, gold rings weighing about two taels, and clothing, fur robes, and other items worth over a hundred dollars. Before leaving, they fired over a dozen shots as a warning before fleeing with the loot. The active bandits in the four townships during the winter defense period are evident.

The Agriculture Promotion Institute in Wuxi County is Abolished 106

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction recently stated that the Agriculture Promotion Institutes established in various counties were primarily intended to promote sericulture knowledge and guide silkworm rearing skills. After the implementation of unified cocoon management by the Industrial Department last year, each county established Sericulture Improvement Areas or Model Areas to supervise the Promotion Institutes and comprehensively manage sericulture improvement. Due to the provincial treasury's financial constraints and the difficulty of funding industrial projects in each county, all Agriculture Promotion Institutes in each county have been abolished. Yesterday, a special order was issued to County Magistrate Yan of this county to abolish the County Agriculture Promotion Institute immediately. All matters that the institute should handle will be managed by the Sericulture Model Area.

Large Number of Buyers and Smokers of Illicit Opium Captured 107

Since the establishment of the opium paste shops in this county, illicit opium has not been eradicated. Many licensed opium smokers purchase and smoke illicit opium. According to the province's regulations on restricting opium smoking within a limited time, opium smokers who fail to purchase the required opium paste within the deadline should be fined an amount equal to the value of the opium they should have purchased. Therefore, Chen Yuchu, Director of the Public Security Bureau and concurrently the head of the Investigation Section, ordered a strict investigation. Yesterday afternoon, investigators Wang Jixiong, Ge Xinde, and Qian Yunlong, led police to the Qian Yunhong sales and smoking establishment outside the West Gate, and the Rui Ji sales and smoking establishment outside the Guangfu Gate. They captured Zhou Tingpei, Xu Genquan, Qian Yuchen, and thirteen other opium smokers who failed to purchase the required opium paste within the deadline. They were all taken to the bureau for fines.

Newlyweds Robbed in Jiading 108

Zhang Bohe, a farmer in Jianlong Village, two li northeast of Caowang Temple in the eastern township, remarried the granddaughter of Li Jisheng, a wealthy man from Chuan Sha Township in Baoshan County, on the 9th of this month. The dowry was quite substantial. The wedding had just ended when, on the night of the 11th, over twenty bandits speaking the local dialect and carrying pistols and flashlights came and knocked on the door. Zhang, initially unaware that they were bandits, opened the door, and was immediately tied up. The bandits entered the bridal chamber to search and rob. The newlyweds hid under the dressing table but could not escape. They looted 300 materials of pearls, four gold rings, and over 200 silver dollars. They also took a cotton quilt, the third one from the top of the bed, claiming that it contained 1,000 yuan in banknotes. Zhang's younger brother, Runsheng, swam across the river and beat a gong to raise the alarm. The bandits hastily fired three shots and fled with the loot.

Local News

The Shanghai Exchange Stabilization Committee Purchases Silver to Support the Market; First Batch Arrives in Shanghai and Deposited in Three Banks 110

Total of 420,000 Yuan; Second Batch to Arrive Soon; Money Supply Gradually Loosening; Foreign Exchange Rates Drop to 11 Cents

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee purchased 200,000 taels of silver from Hong Kong. After completing the formalities, they were shipped to Shanghai in batches. To prevent piracy, the names and schedules of the ships were kept strictly confidential. The first batch, loaded onto the British ship “R威品狄," arrived in Shanghai the night before last, totaling 84 boxes, each containing 5,000 yuan, all in commonly used Chinese silver coins, totaling 420,000 yuan. They were unloaded yesterday under the strict protection of detectives to prevent theft.

(Deposited in Three Banks) The Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee decided to deposit the 20 million yuan of silver purchased in the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications to regulate the Shanghai financial market. The first batch of 410,000 yuan was completely deposited in the Bank of China yesterday. A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency met with Mr. Zhang Peishen, a member of the committee, who said that the silver purchased has been shipped to Shanghai in batches, with the first batch already arrived to stabilize the market. The second batch will arrive soon. (Regulating Finance) The reporter learned from banking circles that the silver purchased by the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee is planned to be fully transported before the annual closing of accounts to regulate the accounts. If the silver and money industries need it, they can borrow from the committee. Since the committee purchased silver and shipped it to Shanghai, the money supply in Shanghai has gradually loosened, and the foreign exchange rates opened by the money market have fallen from the peak of two dimes and one cent.

Sugar Industry Jointly Forms Company to Promote Domestic Sugar 111

Officially Established in Accordance with Company Law; First Batch of 2,000 Bags of Domestic Sugar Arrives in Shanghai

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, Guangdong Province has established five sugarcane growing areas to revive the sugar industry: (1) Guangzhou Area, (2) Huizhou Area, (3) Chaoshan Area, (4) Xuwen Area, and (5) Qiongya Area. At the same time, two sugar factories have been established in the Guangzhou Area, and one sugar factory each in the Huiyang Area and Chaoshan Area. The sugar factory in the Guangzhou Area has been completed and is now shipping goods. The sugar produced is no different from Dutch sugar and is of excellent quality. The first batch of 2,000 bags has arrived in Shanghai, and the second batch of 2,000 bags has been loaded onto ships and is on its way to Shanghai, soon to arrive.

Joint Promotion The Shanghai Sugar Industry Association, in order to promote domestic sugar, has jointly formed the Shanghai Sugar Industry Cooperation Co., Ltd. with its member sugar merchants. It has been officially established in accordance with company law with a capital of 300,000 yuan, divided into 3,000 shares, each share worth 100 yuan. The address is 129 Minkuo Road, Xinkaihe. Arrangements have begun and the opening ceremony is scheduled for February. The board of directors includes Chairman Chen Xinfu, Managing Directors Zheng Zernan, Zheng Yizhou, Jiang Yachen, and Cai Qihou, and Directors Yang Wenshao, Tong Yucheng, Le Ruhua, Chen Lianyuan, Chen Yuren, and Xu Jingfu. The supervisors are Tan Jifu, Zhang Heting, Hu Shubo, and Zhu Gengxin.

Organization of the Company 112

The company's internal organization is divided into three departments: Business, General Affairs, and Accounting. Chen Yuren concurrently serves as the head of the Business Department, with Yang Wenshao concurrently serving as the deputy head. Xue Meiting is the head of the General Affairs Department, and Le Ruhua concurrently serves as the head of the Accounting Department. Considering that the production of domestic sugar is limited and insufficient to meet demand, under these circumstances, the company will also operate Dutch sugar. The organization of the company is the first step in the cooperation of production and sales of domestic sugar in our country.

Result of Negotiations on Fire Insurance in Disaster Areas 113

Chinese and Foreign Insurance Companies Provide 40,000 Yuan; General Meeting Discusses Closure

According to Hua Dong News Agency, the fire insurance compensation issue in the disaster areas of this city has been in negotiation since the Shanghai Incident, reaching three years. With the assistance of the Social Affairs Bureau and all sectors of society, the Chinese and foreign insurance companies agreed to provide relief totaling 40,000 yuan. The Shanghai Banking Association and the Fire Insurance Association received instructions from the Social Affairs Bureau and convened a standing committee meeting the day before yesterday, attended by Tang Youwei, Wang Zhixiang, and ten other people. Cases were discussed and all insured parties were notified. A general meeting will be convened on the afternoon of the 20th of this month to discuss the closure plan. A notice was issued yesterday stating, "It is hereby notified that the fire insurance compensation has been negotiated by this association for three years. Through diligent efforts, we have obtained these small relief funds with the sympathy and assistance of the Social Affairs Bureau and all sectors of society. The total amount provided by Chinese and foreign companies is 40,000 yuan. The Association hereby notifies all insured parties to convene a general meeting to discuss the closure plan. In addition to the report issued by the Association, this notice is hereby issued, Standing Committee of the Disaster Area Fire Insurance Compensation Association."

Brokers and Chairmen of Various Exchanges Discuss and Strive for Exchange Tax 114

Resolved to Request the City Chamber of Commerce to Forward Petition to Central Government to Strive for Cancellation; Telegraph to the Legislative Yuan to Allow Broker Representatives to Attend Review Meeting

The Shanghai Association of Brokers of Various Exchanges held a banquet at the Yizhixiang Restaurant yesterday evening at 7 p.m., inviting the chairmen of the five exchanges, including the Gold Exchange, to discuss how to strive for the exchange tax. The attendees included Xu Bosun, Chairman of the Gold Exchange; Zhan Liansheng, Wang Yingchang, Wang Jiafu, Gao Qiumei, and Zhang Zhusun from the Association of Brokers; Zhang Weiru, Chairman of the Securities Exchange; Wang Zhengru and Wu Limen, representatives of the brokers; Mu Ouchu, Chairman of the Cotton Cloth Exchange; Bian Futang, Wu Xunqing, Shao Wenyao, Zhang Bokun, and Kuang Jian, representatives of the brokers; Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Miscellaneous Grain Exchange; Fu Changyu, Xue Chengzhang, and Xu Jianqi, representatives of the brokers; Wang Yiting, Chairman of the Flour Exchange; Zhu Jiansheng, Xia Rongchang, Wang Zhongliang, and Yang Jingcheng, and over 30 other people.

Various Resolutions Bian Futang, chairman and representative of the brokers of the Cloth Exchange, reported on the impact of the Ministry of Finance's proposed exchange tax on business operations and invited the chairmen of various exchanges to discuss countermeasures. The chairmen, Mu Ouchu, Gu Xinyi, Wang Yiting, Xu Bosun, and Zhang Weiru, expressed their opinions successively. Discussion began and the following resolutions were made: (1) The brokers of each exchange are affected by the Finance Ministry's tax levy, and their interests are closely related to the exchanges. It was resolved to act as a supporter of the exchanges and must achieve the cancellation of the proposed tax levy. (2) A joint petition will be submitted to the City Chamber of Commerce to be forwarded to the National Government, the Central Political Council, the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and other agencies, requesting that the tax be temporarily suspended for the sake of maintaining commerce during this time of economic recession. Other important proposals were not made public. The meeting adjourned at 8:30 p.m.

Request to Attend According to a person in charge of the Association of Brokers of Exchanges, speaking to a reporter from the Da Gong News Agency, in addition to deciding on various measures to strive for tax exemption at tonight's (i.e., last night's) meeting, the brokers believe that the new provincial tax has a significant impact on the future of the exchanges. Therefore, it was decided to telegraph the Legislative Yuan to request that representatives elected by the brokers be allowed to attend the review meetings of the economic and financial groups to present their opinions. The draft telegraph was prepared and will be sent out today.

Trip to Beijing Undecided The chairmen of the five exchanges, including the Gold Exchange, have not yet received notification of their trip to Beijing to attend the review meeting of the Legislative Yuan. Therefore, the date of their trip to Beijing has not yet been determined. According to Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Miscellaneous Grain Exchange, the newly elected fourth Legislative Committee members only took office today (i.e., yesterday). The first general meeting will be held on the 17th of this month. The various economic and financial groups must be established before they can be convened. It is expected that they will be convened around the 20th of this month. The date of the chairmen's trip to Beijing will also be at this time.

Xiamen Bank's Shanghai Branch Still Open for Business Yesterday 115

Deposits Were Only 30,000 to 40,000 Yuan; All Were Returned to Depositors Yesterday

Central News Agency: The Xiamen Commercial Bank's Xiamen head office was forced to suspend operations on the 12th of this month due to a run on the bank. The bank has a branch on North Sichuan Road in Shanghai and an office in Ningbo. A reporter from the Central News Agency, because the bank's branch has been in Shanghai for many years and has had an impact on society, specifically visited Mr. Lu Baomin, the director of the branch's business department. According to him:

(History of the Bank) The Xiamen Bank was established on June 1, 1920. On May 9, 1921, it registered with the Beijing government for a term of 30 years. It is a limited liability company with a total capital of 1.2 million yuan and a paid-up capital of 660,000 yuan, divided into 12,000 shares. Last year, after the paid-up capital reached 750,000 yuan, it submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance for registration. In 1926, a branch was added on Minkuo Road in Shanghai, which was then moved to Ningbo Road. Last year, it moved to its current address. Later, an office was also established in Ningbo. The branch and office do not have independent capital and have not applied for registration. Although they are called branches, they are actually no different from offices, specializing in domestic and international remittances and export financing, mortgage loans and guaranteed beneficial loans, acting as agents for the purchase and sale of securities, bullion, and currencies of various countries, managing deposits and safekeeping, etc. (Reasons for Suspension) The head office's capital is all in Xiamen. The chairman, Liao Zhonghe, and the general manager, Ouyang Ze, each have a money shop in Xiamen, one named Yufeng and the other named Jieshun. Recently, because Xiamen's commerce has declined sharply, the silver and money industries have suffered fatal blows. The money shops were successively forced to close due to runs on the bank. People in Xiamen knew that the two money shops were opened by the chairman and manager of the Xiamen Bank, so they suspected that the bank was also empty and spread the news, causing a run on the bank. The authorities were unable to cope with the situation due to insufficient deposits, so they announced a temporary suspension of operations for seven days starting on the 12th. Now they have extended it to the 15th.

(Branch Situation) The Shanghai branch originally had no fixed capital. However, because the management's skills were still stable, the business was not bad. It is said that the loans amount to approximately 300,000 yuan, while the deposits are only 30,000 to 40,000 yuan. The same is true for the Ningbo office. After receiving the telegram from the head office announcing the suspension of operations, the key personnel of the branch held meetings all night the day before yesterday, finally deciding to continue operations yesterday at 3 a.m. This is because, on the one hand, the deposits are limited, and the branch has sufficient preparations to manage them. Moreover, most of these deposits are fixed-term deposits. When deposits were made at an interest rate of 8%, they can now be returned at an interest rate of 3%, which is actually beneficial for the bank. On the other hand, the loans amount to more than 300,000 yuan. If operations are suspended, it will be difficult to recover all of them. In summary, all deposits were returned to depositors from morning to night yesterday. However, those who still wanted to deposit were refused to avoid adding procedures in the future. The same is true for the Ningbo office. Therefore, there were no losses to the depositors. (Future Plans) Mr. Lu also said that the branch will continue to operate for the time being, pending the resolution of the Xiamen shareholders' meeting.

Ministry of Railways Approves Issuance of Bonuses to Employees of Two Railways 116

Totaling 585,000 Yuan

Central News Agency: Regarding the issuance of bonuses to employees of the two railways for 1934, it was previously ordered by the Ministry to be calculated by the Accounting Department according to the Ministry's calculation form for year-end bonuses and four attached forms, and the amount of the bonus was calculated. It is said that the two percent of the net profit of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway in 1934 to issue bonuses at the rate of one month's salary is short of 64,470 yuan. However, the calculation of two percent of the net profit of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway exceeds the amount needed to issue one month's salary by 57,160 yuan. Therefore, the surplus will offset the shortfall, and the total bonus will be approximately equivalent to one month's salary. The total amount of this bonus is approximately 585,000 yuan. The Bureau submitted a report to the Ministry of Railways on December 24, 1934, which has now been approved by the Ministry's order No. 2626. All offices were immediately ordered to register the employees and amounts entitled to bonuses in accordance with the regulations and report them to the Accounting Department for batch issuance after verification.

The Jian'an Ship Sank in Tongzhou 118

Ship Aground During Rescue and Split into Two Sections; Passengers and Crew Safe; Most Cargo Lost

The Jian'an ship, a Yangtze River vessel owned by the British company Taikoo, was launched on the night of the 11th and sailed to Tiansheng Port and Yaojian Shijian in Tongzhou. Due to the fog at night, the ship mistakenly entered a shallow beach. There were many stone pillars on the riverbank, and the bottom of the Jian'an ship was damaged by the stone pillars, causing water to enter the cabin. On the morning of the 12th, the company urgently dispatched four ships, including the Zhuting small steamship and a tugboat, to the site to rescue the passengers. First, dozens of passengers were rescued onto the barge. Then, the hatches were opened, and part of the cargo was unloaded. The towing and rescue work began on the afternoon of the 13th.

(Ship Split in Two) On the night of the 13th, while the ship was being towed, a certain Yangtze River vessel was launched and passed through Tongzhou. The captain of the Jian'an ship negotiated with the captain of the passing vessel to request assistance in towing. In accordance with the sea rescue regulations, the captain agreed to tow the ship. However, because the Jian'an ship was old and deeply mired in the sand, the passing vessel opened full power to tow it away from the shallow beach. At that time, the bottom of the Jian'an ship hit a reef (i.e., stone pillars), causing the ship's body to split into two sections. The bow and stern separated from the middle cabin, causing it to sink immediately. The crew and sailors each sought escape routes and competed to board other vessels. Fortunately, the passengers had been rescued earlier and were not harmed. The company's Yangtze River vessels, including the Wuchang, also arrived in Tongzhou and assisted in the rescue. The front and rear sections of the Jian'an ship sank in less than a quarter of an hour. Currently, the ship's masts can still be seen slightly above the river surface.

(Loss of Ship and Cargo) The Jian'an ship had a displacement of 1,770 tons and was built in Shanghai in 1907. It was originally used for flood routes in the middle reaches of the Yangtze River. Because of the shallow water in winter, it was changed to the Shanghai-Hankou route. This time, it was launched from Hankou and carried over 10,000 pieces of cargo. Except for a portion that had been unloaded by three barges, sixty percent remained inside the ship, so the losses were quite large. Less than 100 first, second, third-class, and steerage passengers were rescued and brought to Shanghai by other ships, arriving safely in Shanghai the night before last. The total loss of the ship and cargo is at least 200,000 yuan or more. Currently, a ship from the Chinese Navy is stationed at the site of the sunken ship to protect it. The company received a telegram yesterday about the sinking of the Jian'an and immediately decided to send the general shipowner, Guo Lefu, to inspect the site.

The Shanghai-Ningbo Route Will Be Transformed into the Shanghai-Zhenhai Line 121

The competition between Shanghai and Ningbo has come to an end. Yesterday, the four companies signed an agreement to continue their cooperation. However, the route will suddenly be changed to the Shanghai-Zhenhai line. We will restate the situation below to clarify the true picture: (Mingxing Can Sail the Yangtze River) After deliberation by the four companies, the Sanbei Shipping Company's new ship, Mingxing, will fundamentally cease operating on the Ningbo route. However, while the other ships are being repaired, the Mingxing will be formally added to the Shanghai-Ningbo line as a substitute. As for the Mingxing's future formal route, it will operate on the Yangtze River line between Shanghai and Hankou. Based on this principle, the companies will continue to discuss the continued cooperation of the Shanghai-Ningbo ships. The agreement is currently being discussed and drafted.

(China Merchants Also Goes to Zhenhai) This time, the competition between Shanghai and Ningbo has led to the mutual opening of Zhenhai port. Because Zhenhai is an inland port, goods to and from it can generally be exempted from customs duties. Sanbei has already obtained the approval of the Customs Commissioner to proceed accordingly. Therefore, in the future, Ningbo goods will be transported by land to Zhenhai and then transferred to ships to enjoy tax-free benefits. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has also decided to dispatch the new Jiangtian ship to operate on this route. The Ning Shao Company's new Ning Shao will also adopt the same method. In the future, the ships on the Shanghai-Ningbo line will be transformed into the Shanghai-Zhenhai line, with Ningbo becoming a secondary port, insignificant in terms of business.

(British Ships Fall Behind) Originally, among the four companies operating on the Ningbo route, Jardine Matheson's (Taigu) business was the largest, consistently ranking first. Since the cooperation, although they accounted for eleven shares, they still had to allocate and distribute profits to companies with insufficient shares or revenue. Now, due to the Mingxing's price war, the route is being transformed, and Ningbo will become a port for passengers to embark and disembark. Goods to and from Shanghai will gradually be loaded and unloaded at Zhenhai, greatly reducing customs duties for merchants. However, since Jardine Matheson is a foreign shipping company, it cannot berth at the inland port of Zhenhai to transport goods. As a result, after the new route is opened, the business of British ships will fall behind. This is truly unexpected.

The Taxpayers' Association Sends a Letter Requesting the Dismissal of a Lawless Foreign Constable 122

No. 1 Constable Abuses a Vendor

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association, based on a petition from the Fruit Vendors Association of the Shanghai International Settlement, sent a letter to the Public Works Department, which stated: "To whom it may concern: We have received a petition from the Fruit Vendors Association of the Shanghai International Settlement, which states: 'We, the petitioners, are all engaged in selling fruit in the special district, holding business licenses issued by the Public Works Department of the Shanghai International Settlement. We abide by the rules and regulations and have been in business for many years. Although our business is small, it is a legitimate business, and we earn a small profit to support our families and avoid starvation. Last year, we were disturbed by vagrants, which led to the police sending cars to arrest us, making it impossible for us to do business. Fortunately, we received assistance from your association, which allowed us to conduct our business in peace. For more than five months now, the economic situation has been difficult, and we have been abiding by the rules and laws and have not committed any illegal acts. Moreover, our business is based on borrowing at high interest rates. Recently, the police have been dispatching Chinese and foreign constables to various roads day and night to interfere with our business and prevent us from selling. Now, at the end of the lunar year, the business income of all businesses, large and small, depends on this season. The livelihood of several family members depends on this season, otherwise, we will be left to die. Currently, we have witnessed several of our colleagues suffering from beatings by foreign constables, and many are not allowed to do business. Among them, Wang Laifa suffered the most. On the afternoon of the tenth of this month, at about 1:00 PM, he was arrested by Constable No. 195 at the entrance of Songjiang Lane on Zhejiang Road and taken to the police station. Wang Laifa repeatedly pleaded with the head of the police station and was finally released. He continued to do business at the original location at the entrance of Songjiang Lane, but was seen again by Constable No. 195, who not only did not allow him to do business, but also punched and kicked him without regard for his life. Most incomprehensibly, he made him carry his load on his shoulders and paraded him around on the road, making him walk in large circles to Yuegui Lane at the intersection of Zhejiang Road, Wuma Road, and Shilu, and then to Ziyoufang at the end of Wuhu Road, Shandong Road, and Wuma Road, and then back to Songjiang Lane at the intersection of Wuma Road, Liuma Road, and Zhejiang Road. Along the way, he was not allowed to stop to rest, and if he wanted to stop, he would be punched and kicked many times. Later, he was unable to carry the load and had no other choice but to throw the load in Songjiang Lane. He was sweating profusely and collapsed on the ground. Passersby and all his colleagues, seeing this situation, felt very sorry for him and pooled their money to hire a rickshaw to take him to the police station to report everything. The police chief sent someone to Renji Hospital for treatment. Hundreds of our colleagues witnessed this and were deeply saddened. We have submitted this petition to your association, requesting you to forward a letter to the Public Works Department, asking the police station not to oppress us without cause, so that we can conduct our business in peace and avoid being unable to make a living. Everything is true, and we ask you to send someone to investigate, and you will know that we are not lying. We beg you to have compassion and present this petition.'" The letter continued, "We have checked that peddlers within the settlement have already paid taxes and received licenses issued by your department. Police officers and constables should not engage in illegal actions against law-abiding peddlers. In recent years, commerce has declined, and the general public has found it difficult to make a living. Being able to make a living as a peddler is a sign of being a law-abiding and good citizen. If, as stated in the petition, your department's police officers interfere with the livelihoods of these citizens, making it impossible for these law-abiding and good citizens to make a living and driving them to take risks, what benefit will this kind of action have for the police administration? Even from a human perspective, the actions of the foreign constable are particularly cruel, inhumane, and contrary to your department's original intention of protecting good citizens. Based on the foregoing, we believe that your department should be requested to conduct a thorough investigation and order the dismissal of Constable No. 195 to deter others and ensure that citizens can make a living."

Ministry of Finance Approves Chamber of Commerce Interpretation of Foreign Merchants' Responsibility for Not Affixing Stamps 127

Violations of Certificates Should Still be Penalized and Taxes Paid After Punishment; Litigation Should Not be Suspended

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the Egg Industry Association requesting an interpretation of whether certificates without revenue stamps affixed by foreign merchants would be considered valid in court if disputes arose over price fluctuations or even litigation. The Chamber of Commerce believed that if certificates without stamps were not considered legal, the result would be that foreign merchants would evade taxes and be exempt from fulfilling their contractual obligations, causing Chinese merchants to suffer double losses. On [unable to read] of last month, the Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance requesting instructions. This was reported previously. The Chamber of Commerce received a reply from the Ministry of Finance yesterday explaining the matter. The original text is as follows: "We have read the telegram of [unable to read]. According to the Provisional Regulations on Stamp Tax and Article 3 of the Implementing Rules, judicial organs should not suspend the proceedings of litigation when litigants violate the Provisional Regulations on Stamp Tax, but should punish them according to the regulations. In addition, Article 21 of the Stamp Tax Law, which will be implemented on a fixed date, stipulates that when judicial organs discover certificates that violate this law when hearing cases, they should be punished according to this law. Article 22 of the same law stipulates that the persons responsible for certificates that violate this law should still be ordered to pay the stamp tax at the applicable tax rate after punishment. Therefore, if a certificate without stamps is involved in litigation, it should be punished and ordered to be stamped, and the litigation should not be suspended. The second point of concern in the original letter from the Egg Industry Association is not a problem. You should inform them of this approval."

General Assembly of the Mining Association 128

Continuing to Petition the Ministry of Industry to Strictly Prohibit Unlicensed Small Mines; Requesting the Ministry of Railways to Reduce Coal Freight Rates

The National Mining Association held its 22nd Annual General Meeting of Members at its clubhouse on Fuxu Road at 2:00 PM on the 13th (the day before yesterday) to discuss various important motions. The details are as follows:

(Attending Representatives) Those present at the meeting that day included Zhu Yonghe and Xia Liangshi from Datong Coal Mine Company, He Shoukang from Yili Coal Mine Company, Dai Linshu from Huadong Coal Mine Company, Sun Mou and Wang Junshi from Kailuan Mining Administration, Qian Tixian from Pola Coal Mine Company, Bai Yunxuan from Shanxi Baojin Mining Company, Xu Zixian from Jinbei Mining Bureau, Li Zushen from Tianyuan Qiugou Coal Mine Company, Wu Rutang and Li Zushen from Liuhegou Coal Mine Company, Liu Wanqing from Changxing Coal Mine Company, and more than 20 other people. Officials who protect or fail to handle such cases should be subject to appropriate punishment. Resolution: Continue to petition the Ministry of Industry to strictly prohibit unlicensed small mines. (2) Proposal by the joint office of the China Fortune Coal Mining Company and the Liangyou Coal Mining Company that the association petition the Ministry of Railways to purchase more open-top coal cars and locomotives and allocate them to various lines to alleviate coal transportation difficulties. Resolution: Passed and referred to the council for handling. (3) Proposal by the Huadong Coal Mine Company that companies operating along the Yangtze River and in the Shanghai area should cooperate. Resolution: Passed in principle and referred to the council to form a cooperation committee for joint research. (4) Proposal by the Huadong Coal Mine Company to request the association to petition the Ministry of Railways to approve a reduction in the freight rate per ton of coal on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway. Resolution: Petition the Ministry of Railways to reduce the rate based on the principle of joint transportation. After the discussions, a group photo was taken, and the meeting adjourned at 7:30 PM.

Since the heavy fog on the 10th, Shanghai has experienced continuous overcast skies, wind, and rain, making the climate very suffocating. However, the venue was unusually humid, and the participating factories found it difficult to set up their displays. Therefore, the temporary commercial center will open for business at 2:00 PM this afternoon and will welcome visitors from all walks of life to visit and commemorate the event.

Taixing Rice Shop and Xinji Hat Shop Announced Closure Yesterday Morning 131

Business Losses and Difficulties in Collecting Accounts; Lawyers Have Been Engaged to Conduct Liquidation

Amid the economic recession in Shanghai, two major stores, Taixing Rice Shop and Xinji Hat Shop, announced their closure and liquidation yesterday morning due to business losses.

The details are as follows:

Taixing Rice Shop Taixing Rice Shop was located on Touba Road in Hongkou, and its manager was Xi Zhengqing. It had been in the rice industry for quite some time, more than 50 years. Its business was usually good, but after one or two wars, it was difficult to collect accounts in Zhabei, resulting in significant losses. It had been struggling to continue until now, but it was unable to continue. Therefore, it closed down this morning and engaged lawyers Wu Kaisheng and accountant Lu Xiehua to represent the liquidation. Its announcement stated, "We have been informed by Xi Zhenqing, the manager of Taixing Rice Shop, that due to the impact of the economic recession, our store has suffered business losses, and our financial situation is not working, making it impossible to maintain operations. We have decided to announce liquidation in order to close down. We have specially appointed your firm of lawyers and accountants to publish an announcement, requesting all creditors to bring their certificates to your firm for registration within 14 days in order to calculate the amount owed. Debtors are also requested to pay the full amount within the aforementioned period. If they fail to do so by the deadline, creditors will be deemed to have voluntarily abandoned their rights, and debtors will be prosecuted according to the law." It is reported that the amount owed by and to the store is more than 100,000.

Xinji Hat Shop Xinji Hat Shop, established by Kang Qiren in the Public Concession of Shanghai, usually had good business. However, recently, due to competition from other stores and the economic recession, its business plummeted, and it was difficult to collect outstanding accounts. It was unable to continue operating and closed down yesterday. The store engaged lawyer Zhang Deyou to represent the liquidation. Its announcement stated, "We have been informed by Kang Qiren, the owner of Xinji Hat Shop, that the store is unable to maintain operations due to the economic downturn. We have decided to announce the closure and have specially appointed your firm of lawyers to conduct the liquidation. All those who are owed money are requested to bring their debt certificates to the firm for registration within seven days. Those who owe money are also requested to pay the full amount within the aforementioned period. If they fail to do so by the deadline, they will be prosecuted according to the law."

The Rescue Beggars Association Announces Postponement of Admission of Women and Children 132

The Quotas of Various Shelters are Full; Aftercare Measures Will Be Discussed in the Coming Days

The Rescue Beggars Association, attached to the Chinese Women's Temperance Union at No. 3 Waibaidu Bridge, Fude Road, Shanghai, originally planned to start admitting women and children beggars at 2:00 PM yesterday. The registration office, changing room, and bathhouse had also been prepared early. Xie Fengbao, Xia Hengbin, Zhang Shilin, and other staff members had also arrived. The reception room was full of beggar children and beggar women, and they were preparing to carry out the registration procedures when Ms. Liu Wang Liming suddenly arrived and announced a postponement of the admission. The details are as follows:

(Reasons for Postponement) Previously, the association had made arrangements with the Zhou Bihan Shelter, the Futong Shelter, the Xin Puyu Hall, and the Women and Children's Training Institute to accommodate beggar women, beggar children, and the like. It had also obtained the consent and cooperation of the relevant authorities of these halls and various charitable organizations in Shanghai. Ms. Liu Wang Liming of the association knew that the admission would not be a problem in general, so when she was running around to various parties a few days ago, she only worked hard to request donations of clothing and did not think about the admission location. Unexpectedly, this morning, all the shelters suddenly sent telegrams saying that the quotas were full, making the matter difficult to handle.

(Aftercare Measures) Regarding aftercare measures, the association plans to convene a joint meeting of various charitable organizations in the coming days to discuss and decide on the matter. The Rescue Beggars Association hopes to find an admission location and start accepting people within a week, considering the suffering of those who are thinly clothed and hungry in the winter. At the same time, the amount of donated clothing is too small and may not be sufficient for use, so it is necessary to seek donations from all parties again.

(The Situation of the Beggars) Yesterday, there were 16 or 17 beggars waiting to be admitted to the association inside the association's gate, including beggar women, beggar children, beggar boys, and beggar elders. They all sat silently with their hands in their sleeves and tears flowing down their faces. Among them, there were four or five beggars who had been waiting since 8:00 AM and had not left until the afternoon. Upon hearing about the postponement of admission, they either cried and called for help, or raised their hands to wipe away tears, or trembled and could not get up. Their condition was very tragic.

(Issuance of Copper Coins) After the association announced the postponement of admission, the beggars were unwilling to leave for a while. Later, the association issued copper coins, 15 coins to each beggar, and advised them to come to the association next week, and then they dispersed.

(Registration Time) The registration time was originally scheduled to be from 8:00 AM to 4:00 PM every day. However, because the association is borrowing a church, there are various difficulties and inconveniences in practice. Therefore, the registration time has been changed to 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM every Monday, Tuesday, and Friday.

What is the Purpose of Robbing a Car? 133

Forcing the Driver Out of the Car with Box Cannons; Rented at Dawn and Discovered at Noon

The Dongxin Automobile Company at No. 299 Dongxin Bridge Entrance, Avenue Edward VII, French Concession, was suddenly visited by two customers at 6:45 AM yesterday.
