Free Talk

On the Issue of Mutual Permeation between Literature and Science 229

— Zhang Xiangshan

Linking literature and science together and allowing them to permeate each other is indeed a current pressing topic. However, the science referred to here is not social science, but natural science.

The issue of close linkage between literature and social sciences seems to have been thoroughly elucidated in the past, because literature is the lower foundation of ideology. Moreover, recently, engaging in literary creation without even applying the methods of social science, needless to say, such literary works are merely castles in the air. This fact clearly indicates the inseparability of literature and social science. Although the fact that literature is a department of social science is very clear, there are indeed people still talking about the close cooperation between literature and social science recently. Of course, there is no regret, only a feeling that it is "an old saying."

As for the issue of mutually permeating literature and natural science, I believe some people will indeed find it strange to fuse two completely different methods into one, and permeate each other. It seems unreasonable and strange indeed. In fact, this only lies in how to deal with natural science. Of course, we know that Darwin's theory of biological evolution based on survival competition and natural selection cannot be applied to social science, and chemical stoichiometry, cannot be arranged in literary works. However, we believe that we are not so mechanical. Our main purpose is to sort out the themes.

The omnipotence of natural science is no longer a question at present. The growth of human knowledge and culture relies on the development of natural science and is becoming more and more advanced. Our literature today is not something rooted in space. Our literature must be rooted in the real society and strive for the task of cultural growth. In this way, both natural science and literature strive for the growth of modern human culture. The purpose is the same, only the methods and forms are different.

Gorky once said, "The construction of popular scientific literature is an urgent and indispensable thing for the cultural education of the general public. Literary masters must assist practical scientific masters to express scientific ideas, theories, and work in simple and easy forms." Indeed, the construction of scientific literature is the beginning of the mutual permeation of science and literature. As for how to construct it without obliterating the unique characteristics of literature itself, it is indeed an event that should be investigated.

Natural science is indeed bitter, dry, and mechanical, without literary emotion. The abstract truth of a thing does not gain the reader's joy, anger, sorrow, or happiness. Therefore, in order to educate the public with popular scientific knowledge without making them feel bitter, dry, and boring, using the form of literature and taking natural science as the material is the best method. At the same time, the opposite is to use science as a background, as a kind of decoration, which is the worst trend. This trend completely treats science, scientists, and the lives of scientists as the background of old social people's themes such as love, death, marriage, family relationships, and personal problems, rather than taking science as a kind of novel theme. There are many examples of this in Japanese literary works, such as Riichi Yokomitsu's "Bird" and "Doctor," which feature mineralogy graduates as protagonists, and Yasunari Kawabata's "Requiem," which uses mental science as its background. However, like Leonov's "Skutarevsky," which uses the technical intellectual class as a turning point, and Afinogenov's drama "Fear," which describes Professor Pavlovdin, the director of the Institute of Physiology, overcoming philosophical idealism at the age of sixty, and Gide's Doctor Ettyingen in "The Vatican Cellars," although they also use science as a background, they are superior. Although this trend is not a healthy aspect of scientific literature, it is still above the horizontal line.

In addition to the above-mentioned methods of extracting principles, we must also promote scientific fantasy novels. These fantasy novels must rely on scientific experimental, realistic data. Gorky said, "The fantasy of ancient people without weapons has already foreseen the possibility of humans flying in the air, diving in the water, endlessly strengthening land sports, and transforming materials. In our era, fantasy and imagination rely on scientific experimental and realistic data. From this fantasy, the creative power of reason can be infinitely strengthened. We know that although inventors do not "very" understand mechanics, they are striving to create new ideal mechanical appliances. We need scientific literature to help children fantasize, to teach children to think about the future."

Regarding fantasy novels, works such as those by H.G. Wells are very good, but we must avoid committing scientific and professional errors, as well as exaggerated romantic elements and inclinations towards mysticism. For example, A. Yaroslavsky's "Cosmic Adventure of the Argo" in the Soviet Union committed these shortcomings.

Scientific literature not only teaches ordinary people to think about the future in this way, but also, most importantly, gives the general public a thorough understanding of the achievements of natural science in the past. Using the rational image of natural science to explain in a literary way gives religion a most favorable barrier, as "The New Testament" and others have fully utilized. We must also do so, but we must never learn from their absurdities, but rather make it non-mystical, and based on scientific practical explanations, give mankind a new popular knowledge.

The problem of mutual permeation between science and literature as mentioned above is by no means mechanically putting the content of natural science into literature, but rather turning natural science into an easy-to-understand material. Relying on literature can extensively cultivate the public. That is to say, literature digests the essence of natural science, and the two combine into one, reaping the effect of making human culture grow. This problem has now achieved good results in the Soviet Union.

As for some people's advocacy of using natural science methods to deal with literature and describe creation, and that analysis of psychological inheritance can achieve success, I disagree. If so, Freud's psychoanalysis should become the best method in literature, but the opposite is true. Our progressive method is based on social science.

In short, the permeation of natural science and literature is not a question of method, but a question of how to address the theme.

Quick Sketch on a Rainy Night 230

— Xiao Wu

If Beethoven's (Beethoven) allegro symphony to describe the night's rain, is to proper no more. For life depressed. Develop a habit of wander alone on rainy days road without rain gear, silently picking up quiet roads to go, often find many subtle interesting wonderland, get body wet as tearful man back, almost is commonplace. That night, the heavy rain fell on the lamplight as if they were trembling, projecting strange brilliance. When I walked past the middle section of Avenue Haig, and glanced at the stone steps, flower pots, and window lattices in front of the Western-style residences with TOLET white paper strips, none of them looked like wonders bathing in the moonlight. Almost cried out, if it were not for the rain-like columns of rain pouring down without end, there would be no more vivid description. This makes one reminiscent of the gentle scene in the passionate comedy of the woman holding the lamp, and the environment of the fragrant boudoir court mentioned in old Chinese novels.

However, the wind blows the half-closed windows rattling, the inside dark as if something is lurking, mixed with a mood of loneliness and sadness, this seems not a gentle and beautiful environment. Another feeling of terror quickly attacked me, as if this abandoned house had the spirit in the poem "The House Lived In". In Percy Robinson's Whisper Side, he narrated the story of an artist going mad in a British seaside inn and strangling his wife. Perhaps this abandoned house had such strange things happened before. This, not to be carefully thought about further, is already chilling.

Returning home, it seemed that I could still hear the rattling of the windows, and still think of the bleak scene in front of the Western-style residences with TOLET white paper strips.

Distinguishing Characters and Distinguishing Words (4) 231

— Cao Juren

Guest: So, according to you, the writing of modern youth is perfect and without any flaws?

Host: That's not entirely the case. Modern youth being more advanced than their predecessors is one thing, and their writing being perfect is another. Even now, there are still foolish people in Shanghai broadcasting the "Primer of Childlike Enlightenment." Not knowing how to distinguish characters is one thing, and distinguishing words is another. Before the Qin Dynasty, it was an era of using individual characters, and the work of distinguishing characters was extremely important. After the Qin and Han Dynasties, the focus shifted from using individual characters to using words. Simply focusing on distinguishing individual characters is of little use. If one doesn't seek the correct use of words but only seeks the correct distinction of characters, what benefit is there to the level of Chinese of young people? You said earlier, "Isn't this a degradation of the Chinese proficiency of young people?" The word "degradation" is misused. You think that "evolution" means "progress" and "degradation" means "regression," but that's completely wrong. The word "evolution" encompasses two meanings: one simply refers to the changes that come with the times, which is completely synonymous with "history" and "change." The other refers to the gradual change in the inherent qualities transmitted from ancestors to descendants; biological evolution means that the various animals and plants that exist today are the result of changes from various forms in the past. "Evolution" and "degradation" do not inherently imply becoming better or worse. When we distinguish the meaning of words, we should say, "Isn't this a regression of the Chinese proficiency of young people?" We cannot say, "Isn't this a degradation of the Chinese proficiency of young people?" The most ridiculous thing is the widespread use of the word "civilized." For marriages, there's "civilized marriage"; for haircuts, there's "civilized haircut"; for plays, there's "civilized new drama," and then there are "civilized methods," "civilized actions," etc. Everything is "civilized." If you ask about the meaning of the word "civilized," everyone is dumbfounded and doesn't know what to say. As far as I know, even specialized scholars have written books to explain the definition of "Wen Gong" and "civilization," but they still can't explain it clearly. Yet, a certificate, two introducers, a marriage officiant, a few flower baskets, and a military band are enough to call it a "civilized marriage." Isn't that a great farce under heaven! Chinese literati have long focused on distinguishing individual characters but not words, using allusions without knowing their original meaning. So, when new terms came from the West with capitalism, they were used indiscriminately without any consideration. As long as it came from afar, it was "foreign"—"foreign matches," "foreign oil," "foreign lamps," "foreign cars," "foreign dragons," "foreign dogs," etc. And as long as it was fashionable, it was "free," "hygienic," "humorous," or "modern"—"free cloth," "free wool," "hygienic stinky tofu," "hygienic clothing," "humorous perfume," "modern soap," etc. One day, a peddler selling Galgren's medicine was loudly advertising in a train car. He said, "Galgren's medicine can be used this way and that way. To promote our business, our company is selling it on the train at a special discount, only two small coins. Do you all approve or disapprove? Those who approve, buy a bottle and try it." His use of the word "approve" shows the poison of fashion and a lack of understanding of the meaning of "approve."

Guest: Old literati misuse new terms, which is certainly true. But surely, old literati use old terms more correctly?

Host: That's not necessarily the case! All the vague and generalized problems that modern youth commit are still inherited from the old literati. Zhang Shizhao ridiculed vernacular Chinese as inferior to classical Chinese, using the example of "two peaches kill three scholars" being more concise than "two peaches kill three brave men." Who knew that he himself didn't understand the original meaning of the "two peaches kill three brave men" allusion? Old literati loved to use the idiom "each situation goes downwards," thinking that it meant "each generation is worse than the last." Little did they know that Zhuangzi's original intention was the opposite. Old literati loved to use terms like "a du," "Ning Xin," "qi qi," "good weapons are inauspicious," "Haotian is not sympathetic." Little did they know that they didn't understand the original meaning at all and used them incorrectly. The habit of using allusions became increasingly prevalent after the Jian'an period. At that time, literati had neither dictionaries to consult nor encyclopedias to look up, relying mostly on memory. Those with strong memories were valued for their rich use of historical events. But memory is sometimes unreliable, and "using historical events" would lead to errors. Yan Zhitui's "Family Instructions" in the "Articles" section said: "The 'Later Han Dynasty Book' wrongly says that Situ Cui Lie was imprisoned with silver locks. 'Langdang' is a large lock. The world mistakenly wrote it as gold and silver letters. Prince Wu Lie was also a scholar of thousands of volumes and once wrote a poem: 'Silver locks on the feet of the three dukes, bumping into the heads of the secretaries.' This is a mistake made by the common people." There are many, many similar situations. Although later generations had encyclopedias, the method of checking was too inconvenient. Furthermore, the old literati were stubbornly old-fashioned and lazy, unwilling to put in the real effort. When the ancients used something incorrectly, it became a mistake passed down through generations. For example, Yan Zhitui distinguished the mistake of "Kong Huai" replacing "brothers." The reasoning is very clear, but old literati still used "friendly to brothers" and "Kong Huai" continuously. Terms like "established at thirty" and "unperturbed at forty" continued to increase without end. Another example is Han Yu's "Preface to Sending Meng Dongye Off": "Things cannot remain silent if they are not at peace." But the text below says, "In the time of Tang Yao and Yu Shun, Guitou and Yu used them, those who were good at crying out, and they lent them to" crying out. Kui relied on Shao to cry out; Yi Yao cried out in Yin, and the Duke of Zhou cried out in Zhou. It also says, "Heaven will harmonize its sound and make it cry out for the prosperity of the country." Clearly, it's self-contradictory and doesn't form a theory. Song Hong Rongzhai already knew it was a mistake. But I've seen old literati use this nonsensical sentence "Things cannot remain silent if they are not at peace" countless times.

On the Chao-Shan Road 232

— Fei'er

Once again, I passed through the Chao-Shan Road.

A person coming from another country will have their mind confused by the currency system on this short stretch of the Chao-Shan Road. Only after exchanging foreign currency for "Shantou paper" in Shantou does a friend warn you that you need to exchange it for another type of currency, because the banknotes of Shantou bankers are not trusted inland. The flurry of silver coins spent and received when buying train tickets and shopping made this traveler, long separated from their hometown, unable to help but curse the inconvenience. After boarding the train, the bumps of this old vehicle were just like a ship encountering a storm, making one feel uncomfortable all over. Ah, Chao-Shan, which I have been away from for many years, these things you have left for returning wanderers are just like "ancient times."

However, looking out from the glass window, the appearance of the Chao-Shan Road has clearly changed somewhat. Although in the autumn fields, farmers are still working with their upper bodies bare, and under the old banyan trees in the ancient villages, by the dark ponds, women are still washing clothes and rice as before, tall bunkers have been built along the side of the village road.

"Now, bandits dare not invade the villages," an old overseas Chinese who had just returned to the country said with a smile, pointing to the blockhouse.

"No, now many of the villagers have become bandits!" a sincere old villager said, following with a long sigh.

Their conversation stopped. Two road-guarding soldiers passed through our train car.

Turning my eyes back outside the train. Under the blurry vision caused by the train's bumps, the black stones of Sangpu Mountain were still shining brightly in the heat, and the oranges in the orange groves were ripening redly.

Looking at the continuous mountain range of Sangpu Mountain, and its rugged face remaining the same, I thought that Chao-Shan should maintain its original cold dignity.

"I think the oranges won't be stalled due to the recession in Tianjin and Shanghai, right?" I silently prayed to the vast fields.

At the same time, a ragged and haggard farmer appeared on the small dirt road in the orange grove, leaving me with a deep phenomenon obtained from the last sight on the Chao-Shan Road.

Smile (5) 233

— Translated by Tang Xiru from English by Lawrence

They stretched out their hands in bewilderment; he looked for the door, but even as he walked away, he couldn't help but catch the afterglow of the black eyes of that sturdy nun, flashing with its eternal transience, and the smile ran across his face again. At the same time, his heart was thinking, he really wished he could hold her two small dark milky-white hands, like a pair of paired birds, moving affectionately in their sleeves.

He tried to bring his thoughts back to his own shortcomings, "It's my fault!" he shouted angrily to himself. But even as he shouted this sentence, he still felt something tickling beside his ribs, telling him; laugh!

The three women, left in this tall room, looked at each other, they raised their hands for a while, as if six small birds suddenly flew out of the leaves, and then put them down again.

"Poor soul," said the abbess sympathetically.

"Really. Really. Poor soul," the young nun called out with a kind of innocent, sharp emotion.

"Gia," said the pensive, far-sighted nun.

The abbess silently moved closer to the bed and bent her head over the face of the corpse.

"She seems to know, poor soul," she murmured. "Don't you think so?"

The three white-headed heads leaned together. They saw for the first time a shallow, comical wrinkle at the corner of Ophelia's mouth. They looked with a kind of excited strangeness.

"She has already seen him," said the young, terrified nun.

The abbess, with a graceful gesture, put the delicately embroidered cloth back on the cold face; they twirled their rosaries and mumbled a prayer for the dead soul. Then the abbess placed two candles on the candle wicks of the candlesticks, holding the candles firmly with her strong but soft hands.

The dark-skinned, sturdy nun sat down again with her little Bible. The other two moved lightly and quietly to the door and walked into the white, vast corridor, where many dark curtains floated softly and silently, like many black swans in a river. They suddenly hesitated. They saw a lonely male figure, wearing a melancholy coat, pacing in the cold place at the end of the corridor. The abbess suddenly quickened her pace.

Matthew saw them walking towards him, these framed faces, and the fat figures without hands, the young nun following a little behind.

"Forgive me, my mother," he said, as if he were on the street, "I dropped my hat somewhere..."

He made a desperate sweep with his arms, his face, no other man could be more devoid of a smile than he was. (The End)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Saar Plebiscite 234

— Wufa

The Saar region originally belonged to Germany but was placed under international administration after the European War. The 13th is the date for the Saar citizens to freely vote and decide its future. The ballot lists three options: (1) Return to Germany, (2) Merge with France, (3) Maintain the status quo. Voters should mark an "X" next to their chosen option. This kind of free plebiscite is different from ordinary elections because it concerns the fate of the territory and the future of the European situation, making its significance extremely important.

Because the Saar has always been a German territory, the majority of residents are also German. Although there are anti-Hitler factions and opposition from some churches within Germany, considering the Nazi Party's meticulous arrangements and energetic efforts, a victory is likely. Assuming this vote's outcome and its potentially serious impact on the future of the European situation, deep speculation is unnecessary. However, one thing is noteworthy in this vote: the general public is unwilling to easily give up their national rights.

According to a Reuters report from Saarbrücken on the 13th, former German Chancellor Papen, along with his wife and two daughters, arrived early in the morning to vote, waiting in the crowd for ten minutes. The last to arrive today was a woman who traveled from Shanghai, passing through Siberia, spending sixteen days on the train, and arriving in Berlin this morning. She specially hired a plane to rush to vote. At that time, the whole city was covered in snow, and rumors of chaos were spreading in the sky, but the woman disregarded everything and went to vote. Just think about how important this kind of vote is.

Papen was once the German Chancellor, so he naturally has a deep concern for the issue of the Saar's affiliation. It is still understandable that he personally led his wife and daughters to vote. However, it is truly admirable that a certain woman traveled specifically from Shanghai, hired a plane in the heavy snow, and went to vote. Furthermore, the telegram only mentions "a certain woman" without detailing her surname, given name, or status. It can be imagined that this woman is not someone with a particularly superior identity. But her disregard for the long journey of thousands of miles and all losses to rush to vote shows how important she views the vote and, more clearly, how significant she considers the issue of the Saar's affiliation.

Assuming this happened in our country, what would our people think of this vote? Not to mention traveling tens of thousands of miles to cast a vote, even those nearby would probably give up their right to vote in this snowy weather, thinking that many people have already voted, so my single vote doesn't matter. Therefore, whether to vote or not doesn't matter. Our people lack a sense of national and ethnic identity. Unless it is closely related to their own interests, they will not easily lift a finger. This is often the case.

My statement is not without basis. Judging from the previous elections of provincial assembly members and members of parliament, it can be seen that voters mostly gave up their right to vote, which was generally taken over by a small number of people handling the elections. Their own vote has already entered the ballot box, but they still don't know who is being elected. Now, looking at the German people's fervent and serious attitude toward their civil voting rights, it is fitting that Germany, which almost perished after the European War, has shown signs of revival in less than twenty years.

One Year Older 235

— Buyang

After flipping through a one-and-a-half-inch thick calendar and escaping a silver-clad New Year's gate, people's age tags increase by one year.

Grandfather, staggering at sixty, is one year older.

Grandson, ignorant at six, is also one year older.

It was the eve of New Year's Day. The elderly grandfather, who also acted as a loving mother, found a blue cotton robe that his son used to wear to school from a purplish-brown bamboo box. He carefully held it up and examined it under the flickering candlelight. Although there were only a few ink stains on the front, and some mildew on the collar and cuffs, it was not torn. The few moth holes inside the lapel would not be noticed by others.

So, on New Year's Day, one could see the grandson, who usually wore tattered shorts, putting on the cotton robe that his grandfather had prepared for him last night, as if inheriting his father's position. Although other people's contemptuous attitude towards him had not changed, the grandfather, who also acted as a loving mother, had already exhausted all possible methods in his heart.

"Grandpa, the length is just right for me," the grandson asked with satisfaction, pointing to the cotton robe that was half a segment longer than before.

The grandfather's face wrinkled slightly, looking like he was smiling and not smiling at the same time. "You've grown a lot since last year."

"Look, in a few years, I'll be as tall as you."

Raising a hand reddened by the cold, he barely touched the grandfather's beard-covered chin.

Almost as tall as himself. A wave of joy climbed into the grandfather's heart. He stretched out a hand covered in blue veins and affectionately placed it on the small bald head. How anxiously he hoped that his grandson would grow up. If possible, he really wanted to add his own extra year to him.

Immediately, he felt that he was sixty-two years old. One year older, wasn't he one step closer to death?

The joy before his eyes was instantly crowded out of his mind by future worries. One hand unconsciously slid down from the bald head.

The grandson looked at the grandfather's wizened face like a dried chili pepper with bewilderment, turned his butt and walked away, feeling strangely bored.

"If I were to die now, undoubtedly, he would become a stray wild child on the streets, letting people bully him, letting wind and frost oppress him," he thought sadly, watching the grandson's departing figure.

He began to curse that the years had aged him.

But he couldn't help but happily welcome the years that would make his grandson grow taller. He had welcomed them several times before; that was when he was about to marry his wife, and he really hoped that time would pass doubly fast to bring his "good days" closer; and also, after he had a son. If his son were alive, he should be thirty years old this year. He wouldn't mistake that; he was born in the year of the horse. It was the year he made the most money. Because he had suffered many losses in his life from being illiterate, he decided to save money to send his son to school. From that day on, his family had one more student wearing long clothes. At the age of fourteen, he entrusted a distant relative to recommend him to work as an apprentice in a pawnshop in a town, and also found him a good wife. But unfortunately, not long after the grandson was born, the wife died of postpartum disease. Then the son also died in a summer when infectious diseases were prevalent. The grandfather and grandson lived alone like this until now.

Now he continues to sell his remaining labor while projecting the psychology of hoping for his son to grow up onto his grandson.

But he is old, and the rewards for labor are not as much as they were in his prime. He can no longer cultivate his grandson to attend school, and even wearing a long robe is still a remnant left by his son.

In his hope, the grandson has already learned to use his mouth to speak and use his legs to walk. The not-short seven years have made the grandson grow to his waist, and at the same time, a few more scars of life have been added to his forehead.

One year older, two different thoughts surged in the mind of the elderly grandfather who also acted as a loving mother.

Rabbit 236

— Qi Wu

On Sunday, I took the child to the City God Temple. Seeing a pair of rabbits in the bird-selling area, he clamored to buy them back.

I originally liked small animals. When I was in the countryside, I spent all my time on my hobbies. The countryside has wide gardens and spacious courtyards. Besides growing all kinds of flowers, raising small animals is the best thing.

Page 19

Almost every family has dogs and cats. These two animals cannot be regarded as pets in the countryside. They have joined the family group, so it is very common to find cats and dogs proudly perched on the ridge of a moving car.

Naturally, my family also had them.

One dog was a mixed breed. I don't remember its origin. It could guard the house like an ordinary dog and help me hunt. It was already the best dog in the countryside. It was always the leader when many dogs gathered. Sometimes when they fought, the dog owners would often come to my door.

Speaking of cats, it was a very lovely one. It didn't steal food and was diligent in catching mice. When I was reading and writing, when I lit a stick of incense, it was as effective as a talisman. I didn't have to call it. It would squat on the desk like a Maitreya Buddha, staring at me. If I didn't tell it to leave, it wouldn't jump down no matter what.

Once, my friend came to the countryside. I told him this trick. He didn't believe it. When he tried to catch it, it scratched him in several places, but he still didn't catch it.

Enough with the digression. What I want to write about is my experience raising rabbits in the countryside. Country people especially value rabbits. They are unwilling to give them away unless they are close relatives and good friends, so getting ten pairs of rabbits was a very good opportunity.

It was my tenant. Because they found work in Nanjing, the whole family moved. They gave away many bulky broken pieces of furniture to the neighbors, and because of the relationship between the landlord and tenant of more than ten years, I enjoyed the priority for the ten pairs of rabbits.

I built a small house in the backyard and picked a lot of vegetable leaves to supply them. However, a difficult problem arose. Rabbits are the most timid animals. It is said that they will tremble and die when they see fresh blood. I can still forbid my cat from barging into the backyard, but if that mixed-breed wolfdog that knew we had killed a wild duck and dragged it back dared to barge into the backyard with its furry face, ten pairs of rabbits would be twelve corpses.

According to my mother's idea, we should give away that dog, but I was a little reluctant to lose this hunting companion. I didn't listen to my mother and locked it with a chain, and I especially told my family to be careful to prevent it from going wild.

The first two months were peaceful, but one time when I came back from hunting, I bought a few beef buns to feed it and forgot to lock it up immediately. Within three minutes, it had chewed up two rabbits.

The bloody scene made me feel very sorry for the other eight pairs. My mother loved animals as if they were her own children. She angrily beat the dog and ordered my family's servant to take it to my uncle's house ten miles away.

So it was peaceful. The little rabbits were also born. The backyard, except for a few fruit trees, was their world. White bodies, red eyes, leaping among the green grass. My younger brother often played with them, getting his whole body covered in mud.

Now it has been three years since I left my hometown. Although my younger brother always mentioned a lot about rabbits in his letters, he told me that after I left, the cat also barged into the backyard once and was sent to the back village by my mother.

Now in Shanghai, where every inch of land is precious, this pair of rabbits bought from the City God Temple simply has no place to play, and foreign invasions can happen anytime and anywhere. In desperation, I keep them in cages in the bedroom, not knowing how long their lives can be sustained.

Night in a Small Inn 237

— Ruowang

It's late at night, weary travelers, take a rest

Dragging a pair of soaking wet clumsy feet in the snow. A dark figure stepped into a small inn that no one noticed. The innkeeper, seeing a guest come, raised his voice and called out;

"We have a guest!"

This kind of cry with welcoming undertones should have been happy, but I looked at the small room doors one by one with a frown.

"Sir, is this room small enough?"

"Is there a smaller one?"

I stayed in the smallest room in the small inn. The electric light was shared with the room next door, and it was very dim, but the dirtiness of the bed curtains could still be distinguished. Seeing the large patch of water on the mattress, I subconsciously felt that this mattress had a rich experience.

Lying on the bed, there was no warm grass underneath, and the quilt on top was also lumpy. Covering myself with it, I felt that the quilt was made of pebbles. After tossing and turning a few times, I couldn't find a place with more warmth.

The small inn was very quiet. The innkeeper's cry of "We have a guest" was like being near my ears, and the sound of footsteps running on the stairs seemed to shake my bed. I couldn't help but feel annoyed. One unpleasant thing after another flashed before my eyes—the stern face of the boss, the ruthlessness of the landlord... Unemployed people are like iron balls in a golf ball tray, complaining, getting annoyed, hating, cursing, trembling...

Gathering at a Restaurant – Dragon Blood 238

Suddenly, a person walked into the room next door, fidgeting with the paper on the walls all by himself, idly whistling a tune. Before long, a peddler of chapbooks went into the next room. It was the first time I had heard the voice of the man next door, haughtily saying, “I’m tired of looking at these bird books!”

“Buy one to kill time, sir. I also have erotic pictures.”

“Don’t want it, don’t want it,” the man said.

There was a moment of quiet.

“Customer, would you like to buy some melon seeds? Spiced melon seeds!” a woman selling melon seeds shouted as she walked into the room next door. The man didn’t respond.

“Grab some to eat. It’s too quiet living alone.”

“Don’t grab. I don’t know how to eat this stuff.”

“If you don’t know how, I’ll peel them for you to eat.”

Again, there was a moment of quiet.

Suddenly, the woman selling melon seeds shouted, flustered.

“That won’t do. I have a man at home. Don’t” want you touching me. Her voice was slightly trembling and a little angry.

The sound of someone being slapped.

“Don’t pretend to be righteous. Sit here and chat. It’s very cold outside,” the man said.

“Chat about what? Buy if you want to buy, leave if you don’t,” the woman said.

“Who’s waiting for you? Why are you in such a hurry? You’ll still get paid, but you have to sit here for a bit.”

They didn’t know there was someone living next door listening to them, behaving so brazenly!

“Don’t let others see. It’s embarrassing,” the woman said; apparently, both parties were close to reaching an agreement.

Then, the door of the next room slammed shut.

I never thought Barbuss’s “Hell” would be reenacted here. I put on my soaking wet pants and hurried to change rooms, moving to a larger one at the very end, furthest away from them. Once again, everything was quiet, and I could hear the sound of melting snow dripping from the roof tiles.

But the quilt was still very cold. Listening to the clock strike, I couldn’t fall asleep even with my eyes tightly shut. So, resentment, vexation, and curses arose in my heart…

Just as I was about to fall asleep, someone lightly knocked on the door again.

“Who is it!”

“Customer, would you like to buy some melon seeds?” It was a woman’s voice. I didn’t even bother to answer her, burying my head in the smelly quilt.

At that moment, I thought of Barbuss’s “Hell” again, and thought of what we call “humanity.”

Money comes and goes, they run tirelessly. Bitterly cherishing the fact that there isn't half a coin in their bag. Former events are told to future people.

National Studies 242

Ms. Wang Bingmei, Tang Poetry

Hua Xing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Weichuan Farmhouse by Wang Wei

The setting sun shines on the village. Cattle and sheep return to the poor lane. The old man thinks of the shepherd boy,

Leaning on his cane, waiting by the thorns. Pheasants crow, wheat seedlings are lush, silkworms sleep, mulberry leaves are scarce.

The farmer carries his hoe. They meet and speak intimately. Envious of this leisure,

Sorrowfully reciting "Shi Wei".

Ode to Xi Shi by Wang Wei

Beautiful color is valued by the world, Xi Shi will never be obscure for long. In the morning, she was a Yuexi girl,

In the evening, she became a Wu palace concubine. On humble days, was she any different from the crowd? When valued, one realizes how rare.

Inviting others to apply fragrant powder, not wearing silk clothes oneself. The more the ruler favors, the more arrogant the attitude,

The more the ruler pities, the less right and wrong are distinguished. Her companions from washing silk back then, could not return by carriage.

Tell the neighbor's child, how can one hope to imitate!

Shen Bao Local Supplement – Film Special

Hollywood Astrologer Dareos’ Predictions for 1935 (Part 1) 243

— Shu Min

Hollywood stars’ astrologer, Dareos, is once again releasing his annual predictions.

People in Hollywood have known his predictions to be "highly accurate" for the past four years. He has predicted signs of marriage, children, death, divorce, etc. He has also announced in advance the ups and downs in the careers or personal lives of major stars. It is said that his predictions have all been confirmed later. We are not promoting superstition, but many stars in Hollywood, although their superstition is not as deep as that of ordinary Chinese people, deeply believe in this great prophet Dareos. I remember that Shen Bao's film supplement also published stories about Dareos' predictions in the past. Now, for the interest of readers, I will describe his predictions for this year again.

It is said that many film producers in Hollywood must consult with Dareos before making an important attempt before deciding whether to proceed. There are also many stars – both men and women – who regularly visit Dareos' home. They are "part of the family" in Dareos' home. Therefore, Dareos knows everything about them, their hopes, their plans, their dreams, and their secrets. Dareos uses this deep understanding, plus what is displayed in the stars and what is manifested in the crystal ball, to judge their future fortunes. Of course, there are many tricks of the trade involved, but at least it is closer to understanding than our blind fortune tellers who arrange birthdates and calculate annual luck.

At the beginning of last year, 1934, he announced all the major future events in the Hollywood film industry. He announced a total of 61 predictions, of which 47 were confirmed, only two were wrong, and the remaining 12 have not yet been resolved, and it is unknown whether they are accurate. For example, Dareos predicted that in 1934, two female stars, one white and one black, would divorce their husbands. As a result, the white woman was Jean Harlow, and the black woman was Carole Frances, both of whom divorced their husbands. Dareos also said that in 1934, three lovely stars would die. As a result, Marie Dressler, Liliane Tashman, and Russ Columbo all died one after another. He also predicted that Liliane Tashman would meet with an unexpected disaster, and she indeed died in a car accident. According to statistics from Hollywood film magazines, 70% of everything Dareos said was accurate, 30% was wrong, and the remaining 20% had no result.

Now, this astrologer is back to predict all the major events in the film industry this year. Even if we don't believe it, we can listen to it as a rumor. His predictions for this year are:

In 1935, three lovely big stars will encounter tragedies and lose their lives.

England and "television" will make Hollywood feel strong competition this year. "Television" will have rapid progress this year and will invade the film industry. The British film industry will also rise without limit, making Hollywood feel extremely uneasy. Furthermore, many American movie stars will also leave Hollywood and submit to Britain.

Myrna Loy will become a red star in 1935. Joan Crawford will get married this year. Janet Gaynor will also remarry. Carole Lombard will too. Greta Garbo will return to Sweden because her mother is seriously ill, and soon her mother will die. Her own health will also be greatly affected afterwards. Although she will leave MGM and set up a company to make films independently, her former glory will decline day by day and will never be restored. Garbo will not have any romantic or marital entanglements this year.

John Barrymore's family will encounter misfortune this year and will be robbed. According to the stars, John Barrymore will have a strange disaster this year, either on his private yacht or under the wheels of a car. John Barrymore will have a huge British film break. His family life will remain harmonious and unremarkable.

Leon Barrymore's wife will become seriously ill this year and will be on the verge of danger. Leon's own health will also decline, and he may suffer from paralysis. (To be continued)

Film Commentary

Review of "Gambling" 244

— You Jing

Gambling, drinking, rivalry, jealousy, murder, accusation, suicide, revelry, a series of crimes such as debauchery and violence, robbery and fighting, are constantly being staged in a corrupt and decadent society. At the same time, they are reflected on the screen by most film producers without criticism or abandonment, serving as entertainment for stimulation and enjoyment for the general public, even those who personally participate in them to varying degrees.

"Gambling" is this kind of film made in such an attitude and with such materials.

Centered on the love killing case of the goddaughter of Dou Bo, the owner of a New York gambling house, it connects the lives of enjoyment and depravity of a group of idle "beautiful people." Shallow, empty, and vulgar from beginning to end, from structure to performance.

"Gambling" in the United States is said to have been a successful stage play starring Geoff 3 Gem Gambling, and he also became famous for playing it. However, this "Gambling", which is reflected on the screen through the eagle eyes of the camera, is obviously smart enough. Naturally, there are some differences between stage art and film art.

Director Rowland V. Lee's use of a sluggish tone to deal with the whole film is a big failure. Although there are some individual shots, dialogues, atmosphere, etc. that are quite beautiful, they cannot have their extra effect alone. As for the fact that the death of Vina, the victim in the murder case, is written too vaguely, reducing the serious emotions and atmosphere in the development of the whole play, and the use of unnecessary insertions to blur the description of personality and psychology, etc., it especially damages the rigor of the whole film.

The casting of the personalities and figures of the two female characters is quite good, and Wynne Gibson, who plays Maggie, is also better.

Audience Opinions

Opinions After Watching "The Road" 245

— Zhou Hui

Undoubtedly, this is a work that grasps reality, although in many places, the author abandons reality and focuses on the ideal. However, in any case, that excellent style, full of enthusiasm, excitement, magnificence, and the emotions of the anti-imperialist movement, we all deserve to praise.

The director can be said to be extremely successful in this film, such as the six road workers being flogged by the local tyrant, Jin Ge cutting the ropes with his toes in preparation for escape, the tension, and Hong Jingling being teased in the rice shop and temple show, which is laughable. In the first half of the film, which is very difficult to please, the author inserted a lot of gimmicks, making the entire atmosphere of the play not feel boring and dull, but feel pleasant and relaxed. Here, we cannot but say that Sun Yu's ingenuity is unique.

Speaking of the actors, the author has grasped the personality of each person to the fullest, Jin Yan's elegance, Zhang Yi's silent and decisive courage, Yizhi Zhi's coarseness, and Li Lili's frivolousness are all brought to the fullest. Especially "Han Lingen's" "gimmick" helped the play achieve a harvest without being boring.

Other aspects such as the beauty, greatness, and lightness of the screen, the clarity of the photography, and the magnificent song also added a lot to the climax of the play.

The Lang Deshan Father and Daughters Return Home with Honors 246

Mr. Lang Deshan, who has achieved great reputation in the world by using Chinese technology and incorporating Western singing and dancing, will return home by the President Hoover ship from the United States and will arrive in Shanghai at 10:00 AM this morning. Lang's two daughters, Mina and Nisa, are also traveling with him and are scheduled to perform at the Great Shanghai Grand Theatre starting on the 18th.

Two Trivia About "Orchid in the Empty Valley" 247

…Hu Die could not be tolerated in her family, so she resolutely walked out, and her family thought she was hit by a train and killed, but the one who died was actually the maid Cui'er. A few years later, when her son stood in front of her and pointed to her photo and said; "This is the portrait of my loving mother" Hu Die's heart was moved, and tears flowed down, but fearing that others would notice, she still forced a smile. Hu Die's performance here is pure and perfect, this kind of emotional change. In terms of expression, it is the most difficult to perform, if you don't believe me, please try it in front of the mirror.

…Old Gao's wife was unfortunately hit and killed by a train, and she cried loudly while stroking the body. When filming this scene, it happened to be when Little Gao was present, and she didn't know how she blurted out this sentence. "Crying so sadly, it really looks like she's dead…" The whole audience burst into laughter, and Little Gao suddenly shouted that she had been tricked. (Que)

Film Novel

相逢待嫁 (Forsaking all Others) (4) 249

— Su Yin

After everyone dispersed, Jeffrey, Sheber, and Dielun rode in the same car. After Dielun returned to his apartment, Jeffrey and Sheber also went back to their respective homes. When Dielun arrived at his apartment, he cheerfully sang while taking a bath. He thought to himself that this was a happy day, and that Manli was the most beautiful woman there could be. When he finished his bath, and his servant Zhuang Sheng handed him a towel, he felt that his future was stable and secure. He also recalled that night when he told her that he had never loved a woman as much as he loved Manli now. Manli extended a slender finger, pressed it against his lips, and said, "Dielun, you don't need to say that. Isn't there also a Connie... didn't you love her too, and live with her for six months?"

Dielun said, "Manli, that can only be considered something done in my youth, it doesn't count. Everyone has to go through that stage. Connie... Denny... Susie... Wu Qian... they don't matter. Really, Manli, they were just experiences, and you are true love." Manli, after being coaxed with such sweet words, believed him and had nothing more to say.

After Dielun finished his bath, he hummed a tango tune contentedly and left the bathroom, running into his bedroom. He called out to his servant, "Zhuang Sheng! Where did you go again? I'm not playing hide-and-seek with you, why do you always hide?" As soon as he called out, someone knocked on the door from outside. So, he shouted as if he were acting in a play, "Zhuang Sheng, come in! I'm telling you, I'm the happiest person in the world! After my happy days are over, I'll find a woman for you too!"

Just as he was talking to himself, the door opened, but the person who came in was not his servant, but a woman, Connie Barney, still with that disheveled hair, drowsy eyes, and charming dimples. Dielun first saw her in the mirror. At first, he didn't believe his own eyes, and he immediately turned around to face her. He smiled unceremoniously, pushed her out of the bedroom, and into the living room. But he seemed to be hypnotized, and he still followed behind her, following her into the living room. He stared at her with both eyes, as if he were mesmerized by a rattlesnake. Connie kept smiling charmingly at him.

She took a step closer to Dielun and said with a smile, "What's wrong? Cat got your tongue?" Dielun unconsciously took a step back and said, "Please leave this place! You can't come here!" Connie was still smiling, her charming eyes half-closed, looking sleepy. She feigned a languid voice and said, "Oh, Dielun, my darling, I can't bear it anymore. How can I leave you? I was so stupid to let you go. Only after you left did I realize that I deeply love you...

...I only love you!"

Dielun said, "But I'm getting married tomorrow!" His voice was almost a shout. "Connie, don't you know that?" Connie widened her eyes, feigning a look of fear, and said, "Dielun! Really? How can that be! ...I don't understand what you're saying!" She started babbling and fussing like this, her voice getting higher and higher. Finally, she shouted, "I came here to tell you how much I hate you, detest you, loathe you, you shameless thing! Whoever marries you, she has my sympathy!" Dielun also shouted, "Okay! You've told me! Now get out of here! Otherwise, I might just throw you out!" As he said this, he turned around and walked into the bedroom, slamming the door shut with a loud bang. (To be continued)

Shenbao Architectural Weekly

Progress of Domestic Building Materials in Recent Years (Part 2) 250

— Xue Cixin

(V) Steel Windows: The use of steel windows in buildings in our country has only a history of a little over ten years. At that time, everything used was foreign goods. In recent years, sales have increased daily, and domestic manufacturers have begun to set up factories to manufacture them. Although the steel materials still belong to foreign goods, the assembly and manufacturing are all done by Chinese. The price is also cheaper than completely imported goods. However, there are still many aspects of the work that need to be improved. It is hoped that steel window manufacturers will improve in terms of work and parts distribution in the future to strive for excellence. It can be seen that the future of domestic steel windows is bright.

(VI) Door Locks: Door locks used to be foreign goods, and even domestic goods were simple. In recent years, Chinese-made door locks have begun to appear. The appearance is as beautiful as imported products and can almost be mistaken for the real thing. Although some of the parts must be obtained from abroad, if one can strive for perfection, it is not impossible to seize the market. Other hardware materials are also increasing daily with domestic goods, and the materials are all applicable. It cannot be said that it is not a promising industry in domestic building materials.

(VII) Nails: The original iron nails in our country were made by hand. They were crude and not suitable for today's architecture. Therefore, the so-called foreign nails can be seen everywhere. Even the smallest nail has to rely on foreign goods, which is regrettable. Fortunately, in recent years, factories have been established to manufacture domestic nails. Although the raw materials still need to be imported due to the lack of a steel industry, the products made in the country are strong, round, and complete, and can be used. If the manufacturing is continuously improved and persevered, and the output is gradually expanded, it is also an expected thing to rise up and seize the market for foreign nails.

(VIII) Conclusion: The progress of domestic building materials in recent years has only been like this. Think about the main materials in construction, such as steel and wood, are there any domestic products that can replace imported products? Our country has always had wood, but large timbers have to be foreign pine. The variety of colors is also beyond the reach of our country's wood. Although foreign wood has to be transported to our country across the ocean, it is more economical and convenient than domestic goods because it is suitable for obtaining materials. Therefore, there is almost no day when foreign wood can be replaced. Looking back at our country's cultivation of forests, the government has not paid attention to it from the beginning. The difficulty of transportation is even more difficult than traveling across the ocean. Such a big loophole cannot be remedied, which is also regrettable. As for steel, it is even more impossible not to rely on foreign goods. Today's tall buildings and pavilions are built with steel and are all foreign goods. Steel-reinforced concrete uses steel, which is also all foreign goods. Although steel bars and angle iron have been manufactured in China for a time, they were eventually discontinued due to failure. It is hoped that today's strategists will actively manage the basic materials of steel and wood in architecture. Its importance is not limited to a corner of architecture; it is also of great importance to national defense and people's livelihood.

Domestic building materials have made considerable progress in recent years. However, it is still in its infancy. Future progress depends more on the maintenance of the Chinese people. It has been seen that Japanese and European and American architects and engineers always specify the use of their own country's materials in their specifications, even when they are abroad. Is it that their own country's goods must be superior to foreign goods? The relationship between national economy and people's livelihood must be given special maintenance and promotion. Because domestic goods in our country have only made considerable progress in recent years, they cannot reach a perfect level. In addition, most of the architects and engineers in our country are students who have studied in Europe and the United States. They are accustomed to the materials of their country. Therefore, when selecting materials, they often take a skeptical attitude towards domestic goods because of their newness, and they feel that foreign goods are usable because they are accustomed to them, so they fail to fully promote the ability of domestic goods. Therefore, whether domestic building materials can be developed in the future, one cannot but hope for the manufacturers themselves to strive for perfection, and even more cannot but hope for the special maintenance of architects and engineers in our country.

Architectural Jargon (3) 251

— Mei Zhenhuan

I. Regarding things used on the building site:

(Regarding shrinkage, a correction can be found in the 101st issue of this journal. Wood is prone to shrink when dry and swell when wet. The previous statement was erroneous and should be corrected immediately.)

Yangjiao (Exterior corner): The exposed wall. The place where the corners meet. That is Yangjiao. Inside the house it is called Yinjiao (Internal corner).

Muxie (Floated): This is like an old hen. It is not a crab in the animal kingdom. It is a rectangular piece of wood used by plasterers when plastering cement. (About four or five inches wide and seven or eight inches long.) (It is a tool for rubbing the cement surface to make it smooth and clean.)

Xuejiao (Shoe): The lower end of the downpipe (Downpipe) and the place close to the surface drain (Surfacedrain). It protrudes like a mouth. Water leaks out from there. This is called Xuejiao.

Jiaoshou: On the construction site, there is always a chaotic situation. Sometimes the ground is piled up with materials such as wood or bricks, making it impossible to walk. A piece of two-inch by twelve-inch Oregon pine (Oreginpine) board is placed in this place to facilitate transportation. This is Jiaoshou (Scaffolding). The bamboo scaffolding erected during the construction of ordinary buildings is also called Jiaoshou.

Tiema (Floorclamp): When carpenters are laying floorboards (a kind of one-inch six-inch or one-inch four-inch tongue-and-groove board), the first thing to pay attention to is the looseness of the floorboards and the discovery of fine seams. At this time, Tiema is used to make them tightly arranged. Its shape is like the phonetic symbol ㄇ. When using it, knock the sharp ends on the joists, then lay the floorboards, close the tongue and groove, and then gradually tighten them with a triangular wooden wedge.

Modou (Inkcup): Modou (Inkcup) is a tool used by carpenters to snap ink lines.

Suojie (Socket): Suojie (Socket) is the joint of a water pipe (Water pipe).

My View of the Future of Our Architectural Community in the Midst of Construction 252

— Tao Guilin

The construction industry is the central system of all construction. Whether it is food, clothing, housing, or transportation, it is directly or indirectly related to construction. Therefore, if you want to know the strength or weakness of a country, you can use construction as a measure. If you want to understand the precision or crudeness of construction, you can use architecture as a divination. The 20th century is an era of material civilization. The so-called material civilization relies entirely on architecture to maintain it. Everything, such as the dredging of rivers, requires construction. The opening up of roads requires construction. The construction of seaports requires construction. The laying of railways requires construction. Other examples include factory construction, farm construction, wharf construction, bridge construction, warehouse construction, office building construction, business development construction, and all other kinds of undertakings require construction. Not only that, but the development of agriculture, industry, and commerce, the infusion of culture, and the convenience of transportation all depend on the development of the construction industry. The mission undertaken by the construction industry is so important and great. In today's world, construction comes first. Since the end of the Qing Dynasty, our country has suffered from foreign insults and internal turmoil, resulting in immature construction, economic exhaustion, people's livelihood decline, and the decline of national power. When the National Revolutionary Army settled the whole country, the government authorities, in view of the importance of construction, advocated it with great effort. The news media also saw the great relationship of construction and publicized it in many ways. And our architectural community knows even more deeply the importance of the mission it is related to and can still do its job. In this way, with the support of the upper and lower levels, it can be seen that all construction in our country will become more prosperous day by day, and our architectural industry will also prosper.
